Abilify:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b>  (AR i PIP ra zole)<br/>
<b>Brand Name:</b> <i>Abilify, Abilify Discmelt</i></p>
<b>Generic Name:</b>
<b>Brand Name:</b>
<p class="ddc-reviewed-by"><span>Medically reviewed by . Last updated on March 3, 2021.</span></p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is Abilify?</h2>
<p>Abilify (aripiprazole is an antipsychotic medication. It works by changing the actions of chemicals in the brain.</p>
<p>Abilify is used to treat the symptoms of psychotic conditions such as  and  (manic depression). It is not known if aripiprazole is safe or effective in children younger than 13 with schizophrenia, or children younger than 10 with bipolar disorder.</p>
<p>Abilify is also used together with other medicines to treat major depressive disorder in adults.</p>
<p>Abilify is also used in children 6 years or older who have Tourette's disorder, or symptoms of autistic disorder (irritability, aggression, mood swings, temper tantrums, and self-injury).</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Abilify is not approved for use in older adults with dementia-related psychosis.</p>
<p>Some young people have thoughts about suicide when taking medicine for a major depressive disorder and other psychiatric disorders. Stay alert to changes in your mood or symptoms. Report any new or worsening symptoms to your doctor.</p>
<p>Some young people have thoughts about suicide when taking medicine for a major depressive disorder and other psychiatric disorders. Your doctor will need to check your progress at regular visits while you are using Abilify. Your family or other caregivers should also be alert to changes in your mood or symptoms.</p>
<p>Stop using Abilify and call your doctor at once if you have the following symptoms: fever with stiff muscles and rapid heart rate; uncontrolled muscle movements; symptoms that come on suddenly such as numbness or weakness, severe headache, and problems with vision, speech, or balance.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not take Abilify if you are allergic to aripiprazole.</p>
<p>Aripiprazole may increase the risk of death in older adults with dementia-related psychosis and is not approved for this use.</p>
<p>To make sure Abilify is safe for you, tell your doctor if you have ever had:</p>
<p>liver or kidney disease;</p>
<p>heart disease, high or low blood pressure, heart rhythm problems;</p>
<p>high cholesterol or triglycerides (a type of fat in the blood);</p>
<p>low white blood cell (WBC) counts;</p>
<p>a heart attack or stroke;</p>
<p>seizures or epilepsy;</p>
<p>trouble swallowing;</p>
<p>a personal or family history of diabetes; or</p>
<p>an obsessive-compulsive disorder, impulse-control disorder, or addictive behaviors.</p>
<p>Some young people have thoughts about suicide when taking medicine for a major depressive disorder and other psychiatric disorders. Your doctor should check your progress at regular visits. Your family or other caregivers should also be alert to changes in your mood or symptoms.</p>
<p>The liquid form (oral solution) of this medication may contain up to 15 grams of sugar per dose. Before taking Abilify oral solution, tell your doctor if you have diabetes.</p>
<p>Abilify may cause you to have high blood sugar (hyperglycemia). If you are diabetic, check your blood sugar levels on a regular basis while you are taking this medicine.</p>
<p>The orally disintegrating tablet form of this medication may contain over 3 milligrams of phenylalanine per tablet. Before taking Abilify Discmelt, tell your doctor if you have phenylketonuria.</p>
<p><b>Taking antipsychotic medicine in the last 3 months of pregnancy may cause problems in the newborn</b>, such as withdrawal symptoms, breathing problems, feeding problems, fussiness, tremors, and limp or stiff muscles. However, you may have withdrawal symptoms or other problems if you stop taking your medicine during pregnancy. <b>If you become pregnant, do not stop taking Abilify without your doctor's advice.</b></p>
<b>Taking antipsychotic medicine in the last 3 months of pregnancy may cause problems in the newborn</b>
<b>If you become pregnant, do not stop taking Abilify without your doctor's advice.</b>
<p>If you are pregnant, your name may be listed on a pregnancy registry. This is to track the outcome of the pregnancy and to evaluate any effects of aripiprazole on the baby.</p>
<p>Aripiprazole can pass into breast milk. It may not be safe to breastfeed while using this medicine. Ask your doctor about any risk.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">How should I take Abilify?</h2>
<p>Take Abilify exactly as prescribed by your doctor. Follow all directions on your prescription label. Your doctor may occasionally change your dose to make sure you get the best results. Do not take this medicine in larger or smaller amounts or for longer than recommended.</p>
<p>Do not take Abilify for longer than 6 weeks unless your doctor has told you to.</p>
<p>Abilify can be taken with or without food.</p>
<p>Swallow the <b>regular tablet</b> whole and do not crush, chew, or break the tablet. Do not split the <b>Abilify Discmelt orally disintegrating tablet</b>.</p>
<b>regular tablet</b>
<b>Abilify Discmelt orally disintegrating tablet</b>
<p>Measure liquid medicine with the dosing syringe provided, or with a special dose-measuring spoon or medicine cup. If you do not have a dose-measuring device, ask your pharmacist for one.</p>
<p>To take the orally disintegrating tablet (Discmelt):</p>
<p>Keep the tablet in its blister pack until you are ready to take it. Open the package and peel back the foil. Do not push a tablet through the foil or you may damage the tablet.</p>
<p>Use dry hands to remove the tablet and place it in your mouth.</p>
<p>Do not swallow the tablet whole. Allow it to dissolve in your mouth without chewing. If needed, you may drink liquid to help swallow the dissolved tablet.</p>
<p>Use Abilify regularly to get the most benefit. Get your prescription refilled before you run out of medicine completely.</p>
<p>You should not stop using Abilify suddenly. Stopping suddenly may make your condition worse.</p>
<p>Your doctor will need to check your progress while you are using this medicine.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture and heat. Abilify <b>liquid</b> may be used for up to 6 months after opening, but not after the expiration date on the medicine label.</p>
<b>liquid</b>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Take the missed dose as soon as you remember. Skip the missed dose if it is almost time for your next scheduled dose. Do not take extra medicine to make up the missed dose.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222.</p>
<p>Overdose symptoms may include drowsiness, vomiting, aggression, confusion, tremors, fast or slow heart rate, seizure (convulsions), trouble breathing, or fainting.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What to avoid</h2>
<p>This medication may impair your thinking or reactions. Be careful if you drive or do anything that requires you to be alert. Avoid getting up too fast from a sitting or lying position, or you may feel dizzy. Dizziness or severe drowsiness can cause falls, fractures, or other injuries.</p>
<p><b>Avoid drinking alcohol.</b> Dangerous side effects could occur.</p>
<b>Avoid drinking alcohol.</b>
<p>Avoid becoming overheated or dehydrated. Drink plenty of fluids, especially in hot weather and during exercise. It is easier to become dangerously overheated and dehydrated while you are taking Abilify.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="side-effects">Abilify side effects</h2>
<p>Get emergency medical help if you have <b>signs of an allergic reaction to Abilify:</b> hives; difficult breathing; swelling of your face, lips, tongue, or throat.</p>
<b>signs of an allergic reaction to Abilify:</b>
<p>Call your doctor at once if you have:</p>
<p>severe agitation, distress, or restless feeling;</p>
<p>twitching or uncontrollable movements of your eyes, lips, tongue, face, arms, or legs;</p>
<p>mask-like appearance of the face, trouble swallowing, problems with speech;</p>
<p>seizure (convulsions);</p>
<p>thoughts about suicide or hurting yourself;</p>
<p>severe nervous system reaction--very stiff (rigid) muscles, high fever, sweating, confusion, fast or uneven heartbeats, tremors, feeling like you might pass out;</p>
<p>low blood cell counts--sudden weakness or ill feeling, fever, chills, sore throat, swollen gums, painful mouth sores, red or swollen gums, skin sores, cold or flu symptoms, cough, trouble breathing; or</p>
<p>high blood sugar--increased thirst, increased urination, hunger, dry mouth, fruity breath odor, drowsiness, dry skin, weight loss.</p>
<p>You may have increased sexual urges, unusual urges to gamble, or other intense urges while taking this medicine. Talk with your doctor if this occurs.</p>
<p>Common Abilify side effects may include:</p>
<p>blurred vision;</p>
<p>increased saliva or drooling;</p>
<p>muscle stiffness;</p>
<p>uncontrolled muscle movements, shaking, anxiety, feeling restless;</p>
<p>weight gain;</p>
<p>nausea, vomiting, constipation;</p>
<p>increased or decreased appetite;</p>
<p>headache, dizziness, drowsiness, feeling tired;</p>
<p>sleep problems (insomnia); or</p>
<p>cold symptoms such as stuffy nose, sneezing, sore throat;</p>
<p>This is not a complete list of side effects and others may occur. Call your doctor for medical advice about side effects. You may report side effects to FDA at 1-800-FDA-1088.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="interactions">What other drugs will affect Abilify?</h2>
<p><b>Taking Abilify with other drugs that make you sleepy or slow your breathing can cause dangerous or life-threatening side effects.</b> Ask your doctor before taking a sleeping pill, narcotic pain medicine, prescription cough medicine, a muscle relaxer, or medicine for anxiety, depression, or seizures.</p>
<b>Taking Abilify with other drugs that make you sleepy or slow your breathing can cause dangerous or life-threatening side effects.</b>
<p>Many other drugs can interact with aripiprazole. This includes prescription and over-the-counter medicines, vitamins, and herbal products. Not all possible interactions are listed here. Tell your doctor about all your medications and any you start or stop using during treatment with Abilify.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="faq">Popular FAQ</h2>
<p>Abilify (aripiprazole) and Vraylar (cariprazine) are both classified as atypical antipsychotic medications. They help to treat several mental health conditions, including schizophrenia and bipolar disorder. They both affect chemicals in the brain such as serotonin and dopamine to help stabilize mood, thoughts and behaviors. </p>
<p>The main differences between Abilify and Abilify Maintena are how they are supplied, how they are administered, their FDA-approved uses and their costs. They both contain the active ingredient aripiprazole, an atypical antipsychotic, and are approved for the treatment of schizophrenia and bipolar disorder. </p>
<p>The oral tablet formulation Abilify MyCite (aripiprazole) is embedded with the ingestible Proteus sensor that allows patients, and, if given access, doctors and caregivers, to track ingestion of the Abilify medication on a smartphone or web-based portal. The system sends a message from the pillâ€™s sensor to a wearable patch on the patient, which then transmits to the device. </p>
<h2>More about Abilify (aripiprazole)</h2>
<h2>Further information</h2>
<p>Remember, keep this and all other medicines out of the reach of children, never share your medicines with others, and use Abilify only for the indication prescribed.</p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is acetaminophen?</h2>
<p>Acetaminophen is a  and a fever reducer.</p>
<p>Acetaminophen is used to treat mild to moderate and pain, to treat moderate to severe pain in conjunction with opiates, or to reduce fever. Common conditions that acetaminophen treats include headache, muscle aches, , backache, toothaches, sore throat, colds, flu, and .</p>
<p>Acetaminophen is also available in many over-the-counter combination medications with other drugs, including Actifed, Alka-Seltzer Plus Liquid Gels, Cepacol, Contac, Coridicin, Dayquil, Dimetapp, Dristan, Excedrin, Feverall, Liquiprin, Midol, Nyquil, Panadol, Robitussin Singlet, Sinutab, Sudafed, Theraflu, Triaminic, Vanquish, Vicks, and Zicam.</p>
<p>Acetaminophen is also found in many prescription combination drugs, including Butalbital, Endocet, Fioricet, Hycotab, Hydrocet, Hydrocodone bitartrate, Lortab, Percocet, Phenaphen, Sedapap, Tapanol, Tylenol with codeine, Tylox, Ultracet, Vicodin, and Zydone.</p>
<p>Acetaminophen is typically used orally, but can be given intravenously.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>You should not use this medication if you have severe liver disease.</p>

<b>An overdose of acetaminophen can damage your liver or cause death.</b>

<b>Adults and teenagers who weigh at least 110 pounds</b>
<p><b>Children younger than 12 years old</b> should not take more than 5 doses in 24 hours, using only the number of milligrams per dose that is recommended for the child's weight and age. <b>Use exactly as directed on the label.</b></p>
<b>Children younger than 12 years old</b>

<p><b>Stop taking this medicine and call your doctor right away if you have skin redness or a rash that spreads and causes blistering and peeling.</b></p>
<b>Stop taking this medicine and call your doctor right away if you have skin redness or a rash that spreads and causes blistering and peeling.</b>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not take acetaminophen if you are allergic to it, or if you have severe liver disease.</p>
<p>Do not take this medicine without a doctor's advice if you have ever had alcoholic liver disease (cirrhosis) or if you drink more than 3 alcoholic beverages per day. You may not be able to take acetaminophen.</p>
<p>Your doctor will determine whether acetaminophen is safe for you to use during pregnancy. <b>Do not use this medicine without the advice of your doctor if you are pregnant.</b></p>

<p>Do not give this medicine to a child younger than 2 years old without the advice of a doctor.</p>

<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Since acetaminophen is taken as needed, you may not be on a dosing schedule. If you are taking the medication regularly, take the missed dose as soon as you remember. Skip the missed dose if it is almost time for your next scheduled dose. Do not take extra medicine to make up the missed dose.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222. <b>An overdose of acetaminophen can be fatal.</b></p>
<b>An overdose of acetaminophen can be fatal.</b>
<p>The first signs of an acetaminophen overdose include loss of appetite, nausea, vomiting, stomach pain, sweating, and confusion or weakness. Later symptoms may include pain in your upper stomach, dark urine, and yellowing of your skin or the whites of your eyes.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What to avoid</h2>
<p>Ask a doctor or pharmacist before using any other cold, allergy, pain, or sleep medication. Acetaminophen (sometimes abbreviated as APAP) is contained in many combination medicines. <b>Taking certain products together can cause you to get too much acetaminophen which can lead to a fatal overdose.</b> Check the label to see if a medicine contains acetaminophen or APAP.</p>
<b>Taking certain products together can cause you to get too much acetaminophen which can lead to a fatal overdose.</b>
<p>Avoid drinking alcohol. It may increase your risk of liver damage while taking acetaminophen.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="side-effects">Acetaminophen side effects</h2>

<p><b>In rare cases, acetaminophen may cause a severe skin reaction that can be fatal.</b> This could occur even if you have taken this medicine in the past and had no reaction. <b>Stop taking this medicine and call your doctor right away if you have skin redness or a rash that spreads and causes blistering and peeling.</b> If you have this type of reaction, you should never again take any medicine that contains acetaminophen.</p>
<b>In rare cases, acetaminophen may cause a severe skin reaction that can be fatal.</b>

<p>nausea, upper stomach pain, itching, loss of appetite;</p>
<p>excessive sweating and severe tiredness;</p>
<p>dark urine, clay-colored stools; or</p>
<p>jaundice (yellowing of the skin or eyes).</p>
<p>The most common side effects of acetaminophen include:</p>
<p>nausea and vomiting;</p>
<p>headache; or</p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="interactions">What other drugs will affect acetaminophen?</h2>
<p>Other drugs may interact with acetaminophen, including prescription and over-the-counter medicines, vitamins, and herbal products. Tell each of your health care providers about all medicines you use now and any medicine you start or stop using.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="faq">Popular FAQ</h2>
<p>Yes, it is safe to take ibuprofen and acetaminophen together if you need to for extra pain relief. Taking ibuprofen and acetaminophen together is quite an effective combination for pain relief because they work in different ways and have different side effects. But you should only take them together if you need to, and only if it is safe to do so. And you should never take more than the recommended dosage of either ibuprofen or acetaminophen. </p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is acetaminophen and hydrocodone?</h2>
<p>Acetaminophen and hydrocodone is a combination medicine used to relieve moderate to moderately severe pain.</p>
<p>Hydrocodone is in a group of drugs called narcotic pain relievers.</p>
<p>Acetaminophen is a less potent pain reliever that increases the effects of hydrocodone.</p>
<p>Acetaminophen and hydrocodone may also be used for purposes other than those listed in this medication guide.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p><b>MISUSE OF ACETAMINOPHEN AND HYDROCODONE CAN CAUSE ADDICTION, OVERDOSE, OR DEATH.</b> Keep the medication in a place where others cannot get to it.</p>
<b>MISUSE OF ACETAMINOPHEN AND HYDROCODONE CAN CAUSE ADDICTION, OVERDOSE, OR DEATH.</b>
<p>Hydrocodone may be habit-forming and should be used only by the person it was prescribed for. Keep the medication in a secure place where others cannot get to it. Acetaminophen and hydrocodone can cause side effects that may impair your thinking or reactions. Be careful if you drive or do anything that requires you to be awake and alert.</p>
<p><b>Taking opioid medicine during pregnancy may cause life-threatening withdrawal symptoms in the newborn.</b></p>
<b>Taking opioid medicine during pregnancy may cause life-threatening withdrawal symptoms in the newborn.</b>
<p><b>Fatal side effects can occur if you use opioid medicine with alcohol, or with other drugs that cause drowsiness or slow your breathing.</b></p>
<b>Fatal side effects can occur if you use opioid medicine with alcohol, or with other drugs that cause drowsiness or slow your breathing.</b>

<p><b>Stop taking acetaminophen and hydrocodone and call your doctor right away if you have skin redness or a rash that spreads and causes blistering and peeling.</b></p>
<b>Stop taking acetaminophen and hydrocodone and call your doctor right away if you have skin redness or a rash that spreads and causes blistering and peeling.</b>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">How should I take acetaminophen and hydrocodone?</h2>

Never take acetaminophen and hydrocodone in larger amounts, or for longer than prescribed. An overdose can damage your liver or cause death. Tell your doctor if you feel an increased urge to use more of this medicine.</p>

MISUSE CAN CAUSE ADDICTION, OVERDOSE, OR DEATH.</b> Keep the medicine in a place where others cannot get to it. Selling or giving away acetaminophen and hydrocodone is against the law.</p>

<p>Measure liquid medicine carefully. Use the dosing syringe provided, or use a medicine dose-measuring device (not a kitchen spoon).</p>
<p>If you need surgery or medical tests, tell the doctor ahead of time that you are using this medicine.</p>
<p>You should not stop using this medicine suddenly. Follow your doctor's instructions about tapering your dose.</p>
<p>Store acetaminophen and hydrocodone at room temperature away from moisture and heat. Keep track of your medicine. You should be aware if anyone is using it improperly or without a prescription.</p>
<p>Do not keep leftover opioid medication. <b>Just one dose can cause death in someone using this medicine accidentally or improperly.</b> Ask your pharmacist where to locate a drug take-back disposal program. If there is no take-back program, flush the unused medicine down the toilet.</p>
<b>Just one dose can cause death in someone using this medicine accidentally or improperly.</b>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Since this medicine is used for pain, you are not likely to miss a dose. Skip any missed dose if it is almost time for your next dose. Do not use two doses at one time.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222. <b>An overdose of acetaminophen and hydrocodone can be fatal.</b></p>
<b>An overdose of acetaminophen and hydrocodone can be fatal.</b>
<p>The first signs of an  include loss of appetite, , , stomach pain, sweating, and confusion or weakness. Later symptoms may include pain in your upper stomach, dark urine, and yellowing of your skin or the whites of your eyes.</p>
<p>Overdose can also cause severe muscle weakness, pinpoint pupils, very slow breathing, extreme drowsiness, or coma.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What to avoid</h2>
<p>Avoid driving or operating machinery until you know how acetaminophen and hydrocodone will affect you.  or drowsiness can cause falls, accidents, or severe injuries.</p>

<b>Taking certain medications together can lead to a fatal overdose.</b>

Acyclovir:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b> acyclovir (oral) (a SYE klo veer)<br/>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is acyclovir?</h2>
<p> is an antiviral drug. It slows the growth and spread of the herpes virus in the body. It will not cure herpes, but it can lessen the symptoms of the infection.</p>
<p>Acyclovir is used to treat infections caused by herpes viruses, such as genital herpes, , , and .</p>
<p>Sitavig (acyclovir tablet, delayed release) is only for use in treating cold sores on the lips. Sitavig will not treat genital herpes.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Take acyclovir for the entire length of time prescribed by your doctor. Your symptoms may get better before the infection is completely treated.</p>
<p>Treatment with acyclovir should be started as soon as possible after the first appearance of symptoms (such as tingling, burning, blisters).</p>
<p>Herpes infections are contagious and you can infect other people, even while you are being treated with acyclovir. Avoid letting infected areas come into contact with other people. Avoid touching an infected area and then touching your eyes. Wash your hands frequently to prevent passing the infection to others.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not take this medicine if you are allergic to acyclovir or  (). You should not take acyclovir buccal tablets (Sitavig) if you are allergic to milk proteins.</p>
<p>To make sure this medicine is safe for you, tell your doctor if you have:</p>
<p>kidney disease; or</p>
<p>a weak immune system (caused by disease or by using certain medicine).</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or breastfeeding.</p>
<p><b>Herpes can be passed to your baby during childbirth if you have a genital lesion when your baby is born.</b> If you have genital herpes, it is very important to prevent herpes lesions during pregnancy. Take your medicine as directed to best control your infection.</p>
<b>Herpes can be passed to your baby during childbirth if you have a genital lesion when your baby is born.</b>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">How should I take acyclovir?</h2>
<p>Take acyclovir exactly as prescribed by your doctor. Follow all directions on your prescription label and read all medication guides or instruction sheets.</p>

<p>Do not crush, chew, suck on, or swallow a buccal tablet. Place the flat side of the tablet against your upper gum, on the same side of the mouth as your cold sore. Allow the tablet to dissolve in your mouth throughout the day. You may eat and drink normally while the buccal tablet is in place.</p>
<p>Do not give an acyclovir <b>buccal tablet</b> to a young child or choking could occur.</p>

<b>oral suspension</b>
<p>Acyclovir doses are based on weight (especially in children and teenagers). Your dose needs may change if you gain or lose weight.</p>
<p>Drink plenty of water while you are taking this medicine to keep your kidneys working properly.</p>

<p>Lesions caused by herpes viruses should be kept as clean and dry as possible. Wearing loose clothing may help to prevent irritation of the lesions.</p>

Adderall:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b>  (am FET a meen and DEX troe am FET a meen)<br/>
<b>Brand Name:</b> <i>Adderall, Adderall XR, Mydayis</i></p>
<b>Generic Name:</b>
<b>Brand Name:</b>
<p class="ddc-reviewed-by"><span>Medically reviewed by . Last updated on April 25, 2019.</span></p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is Adderall?</h2>
<p>Adderall contains a combination of  and . Amphetamine and dextroamphetamine are central nervous system stimulants that affect chemicals in the brain and nerves that contribute to hyperactivity and impulse control.</p>
<p>Adderall is used to treat attention deficit hyperactivity disorder (ADHD) and narcolepsy.</p>
<p>Adderall may also be used for purposes not listed in this medication guide.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Adderall may be habit-forming, and this medicine is a drug of abuse. <b>Tell your doctor if you have had problems with drug or alcohol abuse.</b></p>
<b>Tell your doctor if you have had problems with drug or alcohol abuse.</b>
<p><b>Stimulants have caused stroke, heart attack, and sudden death in people with high blood pressure, heart disease, or a heart defect.</b></p>
<b>Stimulants have caused stroke, heart attack, and sudden death in people with high blood pressure, heart disease, or a heart defect.</b>
<p>Do not use this medicine if you have used a MAO inhibitor in the past 14 days, such as isocarboxazid, linezolid, phenelzine, rasagiline, selegiline, or tranylcypromine or have received a methylene blue injection.</p>
<p>Adderall may cause new or worsening psychosis (unusual thoughts or behavior), especially if you have a history of depression, mental illness, or bipolar disorder.</p>
<p>You may have blood circulation problems that can cause numbness, pain, or discoloration in your fingers or toes.</p>
<p>Call your doctor right away if you have: <b>signs of heart problems</b> - chest pain, feeling light-headed or short of breath; <b>signs of psychosis</b> - paranoia, aggression, new behavior problems, seeing or hearing things that are not real; <b>signs of circulation problems</b> - unexplained wounds on your fingers or toes.</p>
<b>signs of heart problems</b>
<b>signs of psychosis</b>
<b>signs of circulation problems</b>
<p>You may not be able to use Adderall if you have glaucoma, overactive thyroid, severe agitation, moderate to severe high blood pressure, heart disease or coronary artery disease, vascular disease, or a history of drug or alcohol addiction.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>Do not use this medicine if you have taken an MAO inhibitor in the past 14 days. A dangerous drug interaction could occur. MAO inhibitors include isocarboxazid, linezolid, methylene blue injection, phenelzine, rasagiline, selegiline, tranylcypromine, and others.</p>
<p>You may not be able to use Adderall if you are allergic to any stimulant medicine. You may not be able to use Adderall if you have:</p>
<p>Some medicines can interact with amphetamine and dextroamphetamine and cause a serious condition called serotonin syndrome. Tell your doctor about any other medications you are using. Be sure your doctor knows if you also take opioid medicine, herbal products, or medicine for depression, mental illness, Parkinson's disease, migraine headaches, serious infections, or prevention of nausea and vomiting. Ask your doctor before making any changes in how or when you take your medications. Symptom of serotonin syndrome may include agitation, hallucinations (hearing or seeing things that are not real), coma, fast heart rate, dizziness, sweating, feeling hot, muscle rigidity or shakiness, seizures, nausea, vomiting, or diarrhea. Stop Adderall immediately if you experience these symptoms.</p>
<p><b>Stimulants have caused stroke, heart attack, and sudden death in certain people.</b> Tell your doctor if you have:</p>
<b>Stimulants have caused stroke, heart attack, and sudden death in certain people.</b>
<p>heart problems or a congenital heart defect;</p>
<p>high blood pressure; or</p>
<p>a family history of heart disease or sudden death.</p>
<p>To make sure Adderall is safe for you, tell your doctor if you or anyone in your family has ever had:</p>
<p>depression, anxiety, mental illness, bipolar disorder, psychosis, problems with aggression, or suicidal thoughts or actions;</p>
<p>motor tics (muscle twitches) or Tourette's syndrome;</p>
<p>seizures or epilepsy;</p>
<p>an abnormal brain wave test (EEG); or</p>
<p>liver or kidney disease; or</p>
<p>blood circulation problems in the hands or feet.</p>
<p>Taking Adderall during pregnancy can cause premature birth, low birth weight, or withdrawal symptoms in the newborn baby. Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or plan to become pregnant.</p>
<p>The medications in Adderall (amphetamine and dextroamphetamine) can pass into breast milk and may harm a nursing baby. You should not breast-feed while you are using this medicine.</p>
<p>Adderall is not approved for use by anyone younger than 3 years old.</p>
<h2>How should I take Adderall?</h2>
<p>Take Adderall exactly as prescribed by your doctor. Follow all directions on your prescription label. Your doctor may occasionally change your dose. Do not take this medicine in larger or smaller amounts or for longer than recommended.</p>
<p>Adderall may be habit-forming. <b>Never share this medicine with another person, especially someone with a history of drug abuse or addiction.</b> Keep the medication in a place where others cannot get to it. Selling or giving away this medicine is against the law.</p>
<b>Never share this medicine with another person, especially someone with a history of drug abuse or addiction.</b>
<p>Read all patient information, medication guides, and instruction sheets provided to you. Ask your doctor or pharmacist if you have any questions.</p>
<p>You may take Adderall with or without food, first thing in the morning.</p>
<p>Do not crush, chew, break, or open an <b>extended-release capsule</b>. Swallow it whole.</p>
<b>extended-release capsule</b>
<p>To make swallowing easier, you may open the capsule and sprinkle the medicine into a spoonful of applesauce. Swallow right away without chewing. Do not save the mixture for later use.</p>
<p>While using this medicine, your doctor will need to check your progress at regular visits. Tell any doctor who treats you that you are using this medicine.</p>
<p>Adderall can cause unusual results with certain medical tests. Tell any doctor who treats you that you are using this medicine.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture, heat, and light.</p>
<p>Keep track of your medicine. Adderall is a drug of abuse and you should be aware if anyone is using your medicine improperly or without a prescription.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">Dosing information</h2>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose of Adderall for Attention Deficit Disorder:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose of Adderall for Attention Deficit Disorder:</b>
<p>IR:<br/>
-Initial Dose: 5 mg orally 1 or 2 times a day<br/>
-Maintenance Dose: Daily dose may be raised in 5 mg increments at weekly intervals until optimal response is obtained.<br/>
-Maximum Dose: Only in rare cases will it be necessary to exceed 40 mg per day.<br/>
<br/>
XR:<br/>
Patients starting treatment for the first time or switching from another medication:<br/>
-Initial Dose: 20 mg orally once a day<br/>
<br/>
Comments:<br/>
-IR: The first dose should be given upon awakening; 1 to 2 additional doses should be given at intervals of 4 to 6 hours.<br/>
-Where possible, drug administration should be interrupted occasionally to determine if continued therapy is required.<br/>
<br/>
Use: As part of a total treatment program for Attention Deficit Hyperactivity Disorder (ADHD).</p>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose of Adderall for Narcolepsy:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose of Adderall for Narcolepsy:</b>
<p>IR:<br/>
-Initial Dose: 10 mg orally per day in divided doses<br/>
-Maintenance Dose: Daily dose may be raised in 10 mg increments at weekly intervals until optimal response is obtained.<br/>
<br/>
Comments:<br/>
-The first dose should be given on awakening; 1 to 2 additional doses should be given at intervals of 4 to 6 hours.<br/>
-The usual dose is 5 to 60 mg per day in divided doses, depending on the individual patient response.<br/>
-Dosage should be reduced if bothersome adverse reactions (e.g., insomnia, anorexia) appear.<br/>
<br/>
Use: Narcolepsy treatment</p>
<p><b>Usual Pediatric Dose of Adderall for Attention Deficit Disorder:</b></p>
<b>Usual Pediatric Dose of Adderall for Attention Deficit Disorder:</b>
<p>IR:<br/>
Age 3 to 5 Years:<br/>
-Initial Dose: 2.5 mg orally per day<br/>
-Maintenance Dose: Daily dose may be raised in 2.5 mg increments at weekly intervals until optimal response is obtained.<br/>
<br/>
Age 6 to 17 Years:<br/>
-Initial Dose: 5 mg orally 1 or 2 times a day<br/>
-Maintenance Dose: Daily dose may be raised in 5 mg increments at weekly intervals until optimal response is obtained.<br/>
-Maximum Dose: Only in rare cases will it be necessary to exceed 40 mg per day.<br/>
<br/>
XR:<br/>
Age 6 to 12 Years (starting treatment for the first time or switching from another medication):<br/>
-Initial Dose: 5 or 10 mg orally once a day in the morning<br/>
-Maintenance Dose: Daily dose may be raised in 5 to 10 mg increments at weekly intervals.<br/>
-Maximum Dose: 30 mg/day<br/>
<br/>
Age 13 to 17 Years (starting treatment for the first time or switching from another medication):<br/>
-Initial Dose: 10 mg orally once a day<br/>
-Maintenance Dose: Daily dose may be increased to 20 mg/day after one week if symptoms are not adequately controlled.<br/>
-Maximum Dose: 30 mg/day<br/>
<br/>
Comments:<br/>
-IR: The first dose should be given on awakening; 1 to 2 additional doses should be given at intervals of 4 to 6 hours.<br/>
-Where possible, drug administration should be interrupted occasionally to determine if continued therapy is required.<br/>
<br/>
Use: As part of a total treatment program for Attention Deficit Hyperactivity Disorder (ADHD).</p>
<p><b>Usual Pediatric Dose of Adderall for Narcolepsy:</b></p>
<b>Usual Pediatric Dose of Adderall for Narcolepsy:</b>
<p>IR:<br/>
Age 6 to 11 Years:<br/>
-Initial Dose: 5 mg orally per day in divided doses<br/>
-Maintenance Dose: Daily dose may be raised in 5 mg increments at weekly intervals until optimal response is obtained.<br/>
<br/>
Age 12 Years and Older:<br/>
-Initial Dose: 10 mg orally per day in divided doses<br/>
-Maintenance Dose: Daily dose may be raised in 10 mg increments at weekly intervals until optimal response is obtained.<br/>
<br/>
Comments:<br/>
-The first dose should be given on awakening; 1 to 2 additional doses should be given at intervals of 4 to 6 hours.<br/>
-The usual dose is 5 to 60 mg per day in divided doses, depending on the individual patient response.<br/>
-Dosage should be reduced if bothersome adverse reactions (e.g., insomnia, anorexia) appear.<br/>
-Narcolepsy rarely occurs in children under 12 years of age.<br/>
<br/>
Use: Narcolepsy treatment</p>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Take the missed dose as soon as you remember, but not late in the day. Skip the missed dose if it is almost evening. Do not take extra medicine to make up the missed dose.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222. <b>An overdose of Adderall could be fatal.</b></p>
<b>An overdose of Adderall could be fatal.</b>
<p>Overdose symptoms may include restlessness, tremor, muscle twitches, rapid breathing, confusion, hallucinations, panic, aggressiveness, muscle pain or weakness, and dark colored urine. These symptoms may be followed by depression and tiredness. Other overdose symptoms include nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, stomach pain, uneven heartbeats, feeling light-headed, fainting, seizure (convulsions), or coma.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What to avoid</h2>
<p>This medication may impair your thinking or reactions. Be careful if you drive or do anything that requires you to be alert.</p>
<p>Avoid drinking fruit juices or taking vitamin C at the same time you take Adderall. These can make your body absorb less of the medicine.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="side-effects">Adderall side effects</h2>
<p>Get emergency medical help if you have <b>signs of an allergic reaction to Adderall</b>: hives; difficult breathing; swelling of your face, lips, tongue, or throat.</p>
<b>signs of an allergic reaction to Adderall</b>
<p>Call your doctor at once if you have:</p>
<p><b>signs of heart problems</b> - chest pain, trouble breathing, feeling like you might pass out;</p>
<b>signs of heart problems</b>
<p><b>signs of psychosis</b> - hallucinations (seeing or hearing things that are not real), new behavior problems, aggression, hostility, paranoia;</p>
<b>signs of psychosis</b>
<p><b>signs of circulation problems</b> - numbness, pain, cold feeling, unexplained wounds, or skin color changes (pale, red, or blue appearance) in your fingers or toes;</p>
<b>signs of circulation problems</b>
<p>a seizure (convulsions);</p>
<p>muscle twitches (tics); or</p>
<p>changes in your vision.</p>
<p><b>Seek medical attention right away if you have symptoms of serotonin syndrome, such as:</b> agitation, hallucinations, fever, sweating, shivering, fast heart rate, muscle stiffness, twitching, loss of coordination, nausea, vomiting, or diarrhea.</p>
<b>Seek medical attention right away if you have symptoms of serotonin syndrome, such as:</b>
<p>Adderall can affect growth in children. Tell your doctor if your child is not growing at a normal rate while using this medicine.</p>
<p>Common Adderall side effects may include:</p>
<p>stomach pain, loss of appetite;</p>
<p>weight loss;</p>
<p>mood changes, feeling nervous;</p>
<p>fast heart rate;</p>
<p>headache, dizziness;</p>
<p>sleep problems (insomnia); or</p>
<p>dry mouth.</p>
<p>This is not a complete list of side effects and others may occur. Call your doctor for medical advice about side effects. You may report side effects to FDA at 1-800-FDA-1088.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="interactions">What other drugs will affect Adderall?</h2>
<p>Ask your doctor before using a stomach acid medicine (including Alka-Seltzer or sodium bicarbonate). Some of these medicines can change the way your body absorbs Adderall, and may increase side effects.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor about all your current medicines and any you start or stop using, especially:</p>
<p>buspirone, lithium, selective serotonin reuptake inhibitor (SSRI) drugs (including citalopram, fluoxetine, paroxetine, sertraline, others), tricyclic antidepressants (amitriptyline, others) or other medicine to treat depression or mental illness;</p>
<p>blood pressure medicine;</p>
<p>heartburn medicine;</p>
<p>a blood thinner such as warfarin, Coumadin, Jantoven;</p>
<p>cold or allergy medicine that contains a decongestant;</p>
<p>opioid (narcotic) medicine; or</p>
<p>seizure medicine.</p>
<p>This list is not complete and many other drugs can interact with Adderall. This includes prescription and over-the-counter medicines, vitamins, and herbal products. Give a list of all your medicines to any healthcare provider who treats you.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="faq">Popular FAQ</h2>
<p>It would take just over 2 days for a dose to be out of your system. You should allow for longer (7 days) if you have taken Adderall frequently and at high doses. </p>
<p>The main difference between Adderall and Vyvanse is that Adderall is a mixture of four different kinds of amphetamine salts (one of which is dextroamphetamine) while Vyvanse only contains one type of amphetamine salt, called lisdexamfetamine. Lisdexamfetamine gets converted into dexamphetamine once it is in the body. One advantage of Vyvanse is that it may be less likely to be abused; however, there is no generic form available so it is more costly than Adderall. Because both drugs contain amphetamines, they work in a similar way. Studies have shown that Vyvanse is just as effective as Adderall, and side effects, including the risk of dependence, are similar.</p>

<h2>More about Adderall (amphetamine / dextroamphetamine)</h2>
<h2>Further information</h2>
<p>Remember, keep this and all other medicines out of the reach of children, never share your medicines with others, and use Adderall only for the indication prescribed.</p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is Advair?</h2>
<p>Advair contains a combination of fluticasone and salmeterol.  is a steroid that prevents the release of substances in the body that cause inflammation.  is a bronchodilator. It works by relaxing muscles in the airways to improve breathing.</p>
<p>Advair inhalation is a combination medicine used to prevent  attacks. It is also used to prevent flare-ups or worsening of  () associated with  and/or .</p>
<p>Advair Diskus is for use in adults and children who are at least 4 years old. Advair HFA is for use in adults and children who are at least 12 years old.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>You should not use Advair if you are allergic to fluticasone, salmeterol, or milk proteins.</p>
<p><b>Advair is not a rescue medicine. It will not work fast enough to treat an asthma or bronchospasm attack.</b></p>
<b>Advair is not a rescue medicine. It will not work fast enough to treat an asthma or bronchospasm attack.</b>
<p>Seek medical attention you have worsening breathing problems, or if you think your medications are not working as well.</p>
<p>Advair can lead to fungal infections of the mouth and throat. Rinsing your mouth with water after use can help prevent these infections. Advair is also associated with a higher risk of pneumonia in patients with COPD.</p>

<p>Avoid being near people who are sick or have infections. Call your doctor for preventive treatment if you are exposed to chickenpox or measles. These conditions can be serious or even fatal in people who are using a steroid such as fluticasone.</p>
<p>Do not use a second inhaled bronchodilator unless your doctor tells you to. This includes  (, , , ), arformoterol (), indacaterol (Arcapta), olodaterol (Striverdi, ), salmeterol (), or vilanterol (, , ).</p>

<p> level--leg cramps, , irregular heartbeats, fluttering in your chest, increased thirst or urination,  or tingling, muscle weakness or limp feeling; or</p>

Advil:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b>  (EYE bue PROE fen)<br/>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is Advil?</h2>
<p>Advil () is a nonsteroidal anti-inflammatory drug (NSAID). Ibuprofen works by reducing hormones that cause inflammation and pain in the body.</p>
<p>Advil is used to reduce fever and treat pain or inflammation caused by many conditions such as , , , arthritis, menstrual cramps, or minor injury.</p>
<p>Advil is used in adults and children who are at least 2 years old. For children under 2 years check with a doctor.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Do not take more than your recommended dose. <b>An ibuprofen overdose can damage your stomach or intestines.</b> Use only the smallest amount of medication needed to get relief from your pain, swelling, or fever.</p>
<b>An ibuprofen overdose can damage your stomach or intestines.</b>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>Advil can increase your risk of fatal heart attack or stroke, even if you don't have any risk factors. Do not use this medicine just before or after heart bypass surgery (coronary artery bypass graft, or CABG).</p>
<p>Advil may also cause stomach or intestinal bleeding, which can be fatal. These conditions can occur without warning while you are using this medicine, especially in older adults.</p>
<p>You should not use Advil if you are allergic to ibuprofen, or if you have ever had an  attack or severe allergic reaction after taking  or an NSAID.</p>
<p>Ask a doctor or pharmacist if this medicine is safe to use if you have ever had:</p>
<p>heart disease, , , diabetes, or if you smoke;</p>
<p>a heart attack, stroke, or blood clot;</p>
<p>stomach ulcers or bleeding;</p>
<p>liver or kidney disease;</p>
<p>asthma; or</p>
<p>if you take aspirin to prevent heart attack or stroke.</p>
<p><b>Ask a doctor before using this medicine if you are pregnant or breastfeeding.</b></p>
<b>Ask a doctor before using this medicine if you are pregnant or breastfeeding.</b>
<p><b>If you are pregnant, you should not take ibuprofen unless your doctor tells you to.</b> Taking an NSAID during the last 20 weeks of pregnancy can cause serious heart or kidney problems in the unborn baby and possible complications with your pregnancy.</p>
<b>If you are pregnant, you should not take ibuprofen unless your doctor tells you to.</b>
<p><b>Do not give Advil to a child younger than 2 years old without the advice of a doctor.</b></p>
<b>Do not give Advil to a child younger than 2 years old without the advice of a doctor.</b>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">How should I take Advil?</h2>
<p>Use Advil exactly as directed on the label, or as prescribed by your doctor. Use the lowest dose that is effective in treating your condition.</p>
<p><b>An ibuprofen overdose can damage your stomach or intestines.</b> The maximum amount of ibuprofen for adults is 800 milligrams per dose or 3200 mg per day (4 maximum doses).</p>
<b>An ibuprofen overdose can damage your stomach or intestines.</b>
<p>A child's dose of ibuprofen is based on the age and weight of the child. Carefully follow the dosing instructions provided with Junior Strength Advil for the age and weight of your child. Ask a doctor or pharmacist if you have questions.</p>
<p>Take Advil with food or milk to lessen .</p>
<p>Shake the <b>oral suspension</b> (liquid) before you measure a dose. Use the dosing syringe provided, or use a medicine dose-measuring device (not a kitchen spoon).</p>
<b>oral suspension</b>
<p>You must chew the chewable tablet before you swallow it.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture and heat. Do not allow the liquid medicine to freeze.</p>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Since Advil is used when needed, you may not be on a dosing schedule. Skip any missed dose if it's almost time for your next dose. Do not use two doses at one time.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222. Overdose symptoms may include , , stomach pain, drowsiness, black or bloody stools, , shallow breathing, fainting, or coma.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What to avoid</h2>
<p>Ask a doctor or pharmacist before using other medicines for pain, fever, swelling, or cold/flu symptoms. They may contain ingredients similar to ibuprofen (such as aspirin, , or ).</p>
<p>Avoid taking aspirin unless your doctor tells you to.</p>
<p>If you also take aspirin to prevent stroke or heart attack, taking ibuprofen can make aspirin less effective in protecting your heart and blood vessels. If you take both medicines, take ibuprofen at least 8 hours before or 30 minutes after you take aspirin (non-enteric coated form).</p>
<p>Avoid drinking alcohol. It may increase your risk of stomach bleeding.</p>

Albuterol:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b> albuterol inhalation (al BYOO ter all)<br/>
<b>Brand Names:</b> <i>ProAir HFA, ProAir RespiClick, Proventil HFA, Ventolin HFA, AccuNeb</i></p>
<b>Generic Name:</b>
<b>Brand Names:</b>
<p class="ddc-reviewed-by"><span>Medically reviewed by . Last updated on Jan 14, 2021.</span></p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is albuterol inhalation?</h2>
<p>Albuterol is a bronchodilator that relaxes muscles in the airways and increases air flow to the lungs.</p>
<p>Albuterol inhalation is used to treat or prevent bronchospasm, or narrowing of the airways in the lungs, in people with asthma or certain types of chronic obstructive pulmonary disease (COPD). It is also used to prevent exercise-induced bronchospasm.</p>
<p>Albuterol inhalation is for use in adults and children who are at least 4 years old. <b>Always follow your doctor's directions when giving albuterol to a child.</b></p>
<b>Always follow your doctor's directions when giving albuterol to a child.</b>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>It is important to keep albuterol on hand at all times. Get your prescription refilled before you run out of medicine completely. Keep using all of your other medications as prescribed by your doctor.</p>
<p>Talk with your doctor if any of your asthma medications do not seem to work as well in treating or preventing attacks. If it seems like you need to use more of any of your medications in a 24-hour period, talk with your doctor. An increased need for medication could be an early sign of a serious asthma attack.</p>
<p>Only use albuterol as prescribed by your physician. An overdose of albuterol can be fatal. Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222. An overdose of albuterol can be fatal. Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not use this medicine if you are allergic to albuterol. You should not use <b>ProAir RespiClick</b> if you are allergic to milk proteins.</p>
<b>ProAir RespiClick</b>
<p><b>Albuterol may increase the risk of death or hospitalization in people with asthma,</b> but the risk in people with obstructive airway disease or chronic obstructive pulmonary disease (COPD) is not known.</p>
<b>Albuterol may increase the risk of death or hospitalization in people with asthma,</b>
<p>To make sure albuterol inhalation is safe for you, tell your doctor if you have:</p>
<p>heart disease, high blood pressure, congestive heart failure;</p>
<p>a heart rhythm disorder;</p>
<p>a seizure disorder such as epilepsy;</p>
<p>diabetes;</p>
<p>overactive thyroid; or</p>
<p>low levels of potassium in your blood.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or plan to become pregnant. It is not known whether albuterol will harm an unborn baby. However, having uncontrolled asthma during pregnancy may increase the risk of premature birth, low birth weight, or eclampsia (dangerously high blood pressure that can lead to medical problems in both mother and baby). The benefit of preventing bronchospasm may outweigh any risks to the baby.</p>
<p>If you are pregnant, your name may be listed on a pregnancy registry to track the effects of albuterol on the baby.</p>
<p>It may not be safe to breastfeed while using this medicine. Ask your doctor about any risk.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">How should I use albuterol inhalation?</h2>
<p>Use albuterol inhalation exactly as prescribed by your doctor. Follow all directions on your prescription label. Do not use albuterol inhalation in larger or smaller amounts or for longer than recommended.</p>
<p>Read all patient information, medication guides, and instruction sheets provided to you. Ask your doctor or pharmacist if you have any questions.</p>
<p>You may need to prime your albuterol inhaler device before the first use. Your medicine comes with directions for priming if needed. You may also need to shake your albuterol device just before each use.</p>
<p>Keeping your inhaler clean is important to ensure you are receiving the medication. Clean the plastic actuator with the canister removed at least once a week. Your medicine comes with directions for properly cleaning your device.</p>
<p>Follow all medication instructions very carefully.</p>
<p>Do not allow a young child to use albuterol inhalation without help from an adult.</p>
<p>The usual dose of albuterol inhalation is 2 inhalations every 4 to 6 hours. To prevent exercise-induced bronchospasm, use 2 inhalations 15 to 30 minutes before you exercise. The effects of albuterol inhalation should last about 4 to 6 hours.</p>
<p><b>Seek medical attention if you think your asthma medications are not working as well.</b> An increased need for medication could be an early sign of a serious asthma attack.</p>
<b>Seek medical attention if you think your asthma medications are not working as well.</b>
<p>Use the dose counter on your albuterol inhaler device and get your prescription refilled before you run out of medicine completely. Always use the new inhaler device provided with your refill. Do not float a medicine canister in water to see if it is empty.</p>
<p><b>ProAir HFA, Proventil HFA</b>, or <b>Ventolin HFA</b> must be shaken before each use. You do not need to shake <b>ProAir RespiClick</b> before using.</p>
<b>ProAir HFA, Proventil HFA</b>
<b>Ventolin HFA</b>
<b>ProAir RespiClick</b>
<p>Follow all product instructions on how to clean your albuterol inhaler device and mouthpiece. Do not try to clean or take apart the ProAir RespiClick inhaler device.</p>
<p>Asthma is often treated with a combination of drugs. Use all medications as directed by your doctor. Read the medication guide or patient instructions provided with each medication. Do not change your doses or medication schedule without your doctor's advice.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture, heat, or cold temperatures.</p>
<p>Keep the albuterol canister away from open flame or high heat, such as in a car on a hot day. The canister may explode if it gets too hot. Do not puncture or burn an empty inhaler canister.</p>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Use the missed dose as soon as you remember. Skip the missed dose if it is almost time for your next scheduled dose. Do not use extra medicine to make up the missed dose.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222. <b>An overdose of albuterol can be fatal.</b></p>
<b>An overdose of albuterol can be fatal.</b>
<p>Overdose symptoms may include dry mouth, tremors, chest pain, fast or irregular heartbeat, nausea, general ill feeling, seizure (convulsions), feeling light-headed or fainting.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What should I avoid while using albuterol inhalation?</h2>
<p>Rinse with water if this medicine gets in your eyes.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="side-effects">Albuterol inhalation side effects</h2>
<p>Get emergency medical help if you have <b>signs of an allergic reaction to albuterol</b>: hives; difficult breathing; swelling of your face, lips, tongue, or throat.</p>
<b>signs of an allergic reaction to albuterol</b>
<p>Call your doctor at once if you have:</p>
<p>wheezing, choking, or other breathing problems after using this medicine;</p>
<p>chest pain, fast heart rate, pounding heartbeats or fluttering in your chest;</p>
<p>pain or burning when you urinate;</p>
<p>increased thirst, increased urination, hunger, dry mouth, fruity breath odor, drowsiness, dry skin, blurred vision, weight loss; or</p>
<p>signs of low potassium - leg cramps, constipation, irregular heartbeats, fluttering in your chest, extreme thirst, increased urination, numbness or tingling, muscle weakness or limp feeling.</p>
<p>Common albuterol side effects may include:</p>
<p>chest pain, fast or pounding heartbeats;</p>
<p>upset stomach, vomiting;</p>
<p>painful urination;</p>
<p>dizziness;</p>
<p>feeling shaky or nervous;</p>
<p>headache, back pain, body aches; or</p>
<p>cough, sore throat, sinus pain, runny or stuffy nose.</p>
<p>This is not a complete list of side effects and others may occur. Call your doctor for medical advice about side effects. You may report side effects to FDA at 1-800-FDA-1088.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="interactions">What other drugs will affect albuterol inhalation?</h2>
<p>Tell your doctor about all your current medicines and any you start or stop using, especially:</p>
<p>any other inhaled medicines or bronchodilators;</p>
<p>digoxin;</p>
<p>a diuretic or "water pill";</p>
<p>an antidepressant - amitriptyline, desipramine, imipramine, doxepin, nortriptyline, and others;</p>

Aldactone:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b>  (spir ON oh LAK tone)<br/>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is Aldactone?</h2>
<p>Aldactone () is a potassium-sparing diuretic (water pill) that prevents your body from absorbing too much salt and keeps your potassium levels from getting too low.</p>
<p>Aldactone is used to treat ,  (hypertension), or  ( levels in the blood).</p>
<p>Aldactone also treats  in people with congestive heart failure,  of the liver, or a kidney disorder called .</p>
<p>Aldactone is also used to diagnose or treat a condition in which you have too much aldosterone in your body. Aldosterone is a hormone produced by your adrenal glands to help regulate the salt and water balance in your body.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>You should use Aldactone with caution if you have kidney problems, high levels of potassium in your blood, , if you are unable to urinate, or if you are also taking eplerenone.</p>
<p>Aldactone has caused tumors in animals but it is not known whether this could occur in people. Do not use this medicine for any condition that has not been checked by your doctor.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not use Aldactone if you are allergic to spironolactone, or if you have:</p>
<p>Addison's disease (an adrenal gland disorder);</p>
<p>high levels of potassium in your blood ();</p>
<p>if you are unable to urinate; or</p>
<p>if you are also taking eplerenone.</p>
<p>To make sure Aldactone is safe for you, tell your doctor if you have:</p>
<p>an electrolyte imbalance (such as low levels of calcium, magnesium, or sodium in your blood);</p>
<p>kidney disease;</p>
<p>; or</p>
<p>heart disease.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or plan to become pregnant. Having congestive heart failure, cirrhosis, or uncontrolled high blood pressure during pregnancy may lead to medical problems in the mother or the baby. <b>Your doctor should decide whether you take Aldactone if you are pregnant.</b></p>
<b>Your doctor should decide whether you take Aldactone if you are pregnant.</b>
<p>It may not be safe to breastfeed while using this medicine. Ask your doctor about any risk.</p>
<h2>How should I take Aldactone?</h2>
<p>Take Aldactone exactly as prescribed by your doctor. Follow all directions on your prescription label and read all medication guides or instruction sheets. Your doctor may occasionally change your dose.</p>
<p>Do not share this medicine with another person, even if they have the same symptoms you have.</p>
<p>You may take Aldactone with or without food, but take it the same way each time.</p>
<p>You will need frequent medical tests.</p>
<p>This medicine can affect the results of certain medical tests. Tell any doctor who treats you that you are using Aldactone.</p>
<p>If you need surgery, tell your surgeon you currently use this medicine. You may need to stop for a short time.</p>
<p>If you are being treated for high blood pressure, keep using this medication even if you feel well. High blood pressure often has no symptoms. You may need to use blood pressure medication for the rest of your life.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from heat, light, and moisture.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">Dosing information</h2>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose of Aldactone for Edema:</b></p>

<p><b>Usual Adult Dose of Aldactone for Hypertension:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose of Aldactone for Hypertension:</b>
<p>Initial dose: 50 to 100 mg orally per day in single or divided doses</p>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose for Congestive Heart Failure:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose for Congestive Heart Failure:</b>
<p>Initial dose: 25 mg orally once a day assuming serum potassium is less than or equal to 5 mEq/L and serum creatinine is less than or equal to 2.5 mg/dL</p>

<b>Usual Adult Dose for Primary Hyperaldosteronism:</b>
<p>Diagnostic dose:</p>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose for Hypokalemia:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose for Hypokalemia:</b>
<p>25 to 100 mg orally per day</p>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Take the medicine as soon as you can, but skip the missed dose if it is almost time for your next dose. Do not take two doses at one time.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What to avoid</h2>
<p>Drinking alcohol can increase certain side effects.</p>
<p>Do not use potassium supplements or salt substitutes, unless your doctor has told you to.</p>
<p>Avoid a diet high in salt. Too much salt will cause your body to retain water and can make this medication less effective.</p>
<p>Avoid driving or hazardous activity until you know how this medicine will affect you. Your reactions could be impaired. Avoid getting up too fast from a sitting or lying position, or you may feel dizzy.</p>

Alendronate:

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is alendronate?</h2>
<p>Alendronate is used to treat  caused by , steroid use, or gonadal failure.  alendronate is for use when you have a high risk of  due to osteoporosis.</p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>You should not take alendronate if you have problems with your esophagus, or low levels of calcium in your blood.</p>
<p>Do not take alendronate if you cannot sit upright or stand for at least 30 minutes after taking the medicine.</p>
<p>Alendronate can cause serious problems in the stomach or esophagus. <b>Stop using alendronate and call your doctor at once if you have chest pain, new or worsening heartburn, or pain when swallowing.</b></p>
<b>Stop using alendronate and call your doctor at once if you have chest pain, new or worsening heartburn, or pain when swallowing.</b>
<p>Also call your doctor if you have muscle spasms,  or tingling (in hands and feet or around the mouth), new or unusual hip pain, or severe pain in your joints, bones, or muscles.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not take alendronate if you are allergic to it, or if you have:</p>
<p>low levels of calcium in your blood (); or</p>

<p>Do not take alendronate if you cannot sit upright or stand for at least 30 minutes. Alendronate can cause serious problems in the stomach or esophagus. You must stay upright for at least 30 minutes after taking  alendronate.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if you have ever had:</p>

<p>problems with your stomach or digestion;</p>

<p>kidney disease; or</p>
<p>any condition that makes it hard for your body to absorb nutrients from food (malabsorption).</p>
<p>The effervescent tablet contains a lot of sodium. Tell your doctor if you are on a low-salt diet before using this form of alendronate.</p>
<p>This medicine may cause jaw bone problems (). The risk is highest in people with cancer, blood cell disorders, pre-existing dental problems, or people treated with steroids, , or radiation. Ask your doctor about your own risk.</p>
<p>It is not known whether this medicine will harm an unborn baby. Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or trying to become pregnant. <b>Stop using the medicine and tell your doctor right away if you become pregnant.</b></p>
<b>Stop using the medicine and tell your doctor right away if you become pregnant.</b>
<p>It may not be safe to breastfeed while using this medicine. Ask your doctor about any risk.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">How should I take alendronate?</h2>
<p>Follow all directions on your prescription label and read all medication guides or instruction sheets. Use the medicine exactly as directed.</p>
<p>Alendronate is taken either once daily or once per week. Follow your doctor's dosing instructions very carefully.</p>
<p>Take alendronate first thing in the morning, at least 30 minutes before you eat or drink anything or take any other medicine. If you take alendronate only once per week, take it on the same day each week and always first thing in the morning.</p>
<p>Take with a full glass (6 to 8 ounces) of plain water. Do not use coffee, tea, soda, juice, or mineral water. Do not eat or drink anything other than plain water.</p>
<p>Measure liquid medicine carefully. Use the dosing syringe provided, or use a medicine dose-measuring device (not a kitchen spoon).</p>
<p>Do not crush, chew, or suck on an alendronate <b>regular tablet.</b> Swallow it whole.</p>
<b>regular tablet.</b>
<p>Dissolve the effervescent tablet in at least 4 ounces of water (at room temperature, not hot or cold). Let the tablet dissolve for 5 minutes. Stir this mixture for 10 seconds and drink all of it right away. Add a little more water to the glass, swirl gently and drink right away.</p>
<p><b>For at least 30 minutes after taking alendronate:</b></p>

<p>Alendronate is only part of a complete program of treatment that may also include diet changes, exercise, bone mineral density testing, and taking calcium and vitamin supplements. Follow your doctor's instructions very closely.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture and heat. Keep unused effervescent tablets in the foil blister pack.</p>
<p>Your doctor will determine how long to treat you with this medicine. Alendronate is often given for only 3 to 5 years.</p>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Once-daily dosing: If you forget to take alendronate first thing in the morning, do not take it later in the day. Wait until the following morning and skip the missed dose. Do not take two (2) doses in one day.</p>
<p>Once-per-week dosing: If you forget to take alendronate on your scheduled day, take it first thing in the morning on the day after you remember the missed dose. Then return to your regular weekly schedule on your chosen dose day. Do not take 2 doses in one day.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Drink a full glass of milk and seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222. <b>Do not make yourself vomit and do not lie down.</b></p>
<b>Do not make yourself vomit and do not lie down.</b>

<p>Avoid taking any other medicines for at least 30 minutes after taking alendronate. This includes , calcium, and . Some medicines can make it harder for your body to absorb alendronate.</p>
<p>Avoid , or try to quit. Smoking can reduce your bone mineral density, making fractures more likely.</p>

Aleve:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b>  (na PROX en)<br/>
<b>Brand Name:</b> <i>Aleve, EC-Naprosyn, Flanax Pain Reliever, Midol Extended Relief, Naprelan 375, Naprosyn</i></p>
<b>Generic Name:</b>
<b>Brand Name:</b>
<p class="ddc-reviewed-by"><span>Medically reviewed by . Last updated on Feb 3, 2021.</span></p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is Aleve?</h2>
<p>Aleve (naproxen) is a  (NSAID). Naproxen works by reducing hormones that cause inflammation and pain in the body.</p>
<p>Aleve is used to temporarily relieve minor aches and pains due to , muscular aches, backache, , headache, toothache,and the . Aleve is also used to temporarily reduce fever.</p>
<p>Aleve may also be used for purposes not listed in this medication guide.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>You should not use Aleve if you have a history of allergic reaction to aspirin or other NSAID (nonsteroidal anti-inflammatory drug).</p>
<p>Naproxen can increase your risk of fatal heart attack or stroke, especially if you use it long term or take high doses, or if you have heart disease. Even people without heart disease or risk factors could have a stroke or heart attack while taking this medicine.</p>
<p>Do not use this medicine just before or after heart bypass surgery (coronary artery bypass graft, or CABG).</p>
<p>Get emergency medical help if you have chest pain, weakness, shortness of breath, slurred speech, or problems with vision or balance.</p>
<p>Aleve may also cause stomach or intestinal bleeding, which can be fatal. These conditions can occur without warning while you are using naproxen, especially in older adults.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>Aleve may also cause stomach or intestinal bleeding, which can be fatal. These conditions can occur without warning while you are using naproxen, especially in older adults.</p>
<p>You should not use Aleve if you are allergic to naproxen, or if you have ever had an asthma attack or severe allergic reaction after taking aspirin or an NSAID.</p>
<p>Ask a doctor before giving Aleve to a child younger than 12 years old.</p>
<p>Ask a doctor or pharmacist if it is safe for you to use this medicine if you have:</p>
<p>heart disease, high blood pressure, high cholesterol, diabetes, or if you smoke;</p>
<p>a history of heart attack, stroke, or blood clot;</p>
<p>a history of stomach ulcers or bleeding;</p>
<p>asthma;</p>
<p>liver or kidney disease;</p>
<p>fluid retention: or</p>
<p>if you take aspirin to prevent heart attack or stroke.</p>
<p><b>If you are pregnant, you should not take Aleve unless your doctor tells you to.</b> Taking a NSAID during the last 20 weeks of pregnancy can cause serious heart or kidney problems in the unborn baby and possible complications with your pregnancy.</p>
<b>If you are pregnant, you should not take Aleve unless your doctor tells you to.</b>
<p>It may not be safe to breastfeed while using Aleve. Ask your doctor about any risk.</p>
<p>Aleve is not approved for use by anyone younger than 2 years old. <b>Do not give this medicine to a child without medical advice.</b></p>
<b>Do not give this medicine to a child without medical advice.</b>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">How should I take Aleve?</h2>
<p>Use Aleve exactly as directed on the label, or as prescribed by your doctor. Do not take this medicine in larger amounts or for longer than recommended. Use the lowest dose that is effective in treating your condition.</p>
<p>If a child is using this medicine, tell your doctor if the child has any changes in weight. Naproxen doses are based on weight in children, and any changes may affect your child's dose.</p>
<p>If you use Aleve long-term, you may need frequent medical tests.</p>
<p>This medicine can cause unusual results with certain medical tests. Tell any doctor who treats you that you are using Aleve.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture, heat, and light. Keep the bottle tightly closed when not in use.</p>
<p>Read all patient information, medication guides, and instruction sheets provided to you. Ask your doctor or pharmacist if you have any questions.</p>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Since Aleve is sometimes used only when needed, you may not be on a dosing schedule. If you are on a schedule, use the missed dose as soon as you remember. Skip the missed dose if it is almost time for your next scheduled dose. Do not use extra medicine to make up the missed dose.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What to avoid</h2>
<p>Avoid drinking alcohol. It may increase your risk of stomach bleeding.</p>
<p>Avoid taking aspirin unless your doctor tells you to.</p>
<p>Ask your doctor before taking any other medication for pain, arthritis, fever, or swelling. Many medicines available over the counter contain aspirin, salicylates, or other medicines similar to naproxen (such as ibuprofen or ketoprofen). Taking certain products together can cause you to get too much of this type of medication.</p>
<p>Ask your doctor before using an antacid, and use only the type your doctor recommends. Some antacids can make it harder for your body to absorb Aleve.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="side-effects">Aleve side effects</h2>
<p>Get emergency medical help if you have <b>signs of an allergic reaction to Aleve:</b> sneezing, runny or stuffy nose; wheezing or trouble breathing; hives; swelling of your face, lips, tongue, or throat.</p>
<b>signs of an allergic reaction to Aleve:</b>
<p>Get emergency medical help if you have <b>signs of a heart attack or stroke:</b> chest pain spreading to your jaw or shoulder, sudden numbness or weakness on one side of the body, slurred speech, feeling short of breath.</p>
<b>signs of a heart attack or stroke:</b>
<p>Stop using Aleve and call your doctor at once if you have:</p>
<p>shortness of breath (even with mild exertion);</p>
<p>swelling or rapid weight gain;</p>
<p>the first sign of any skin rash, no matter how mild;</p>
<p><b>signs of stomach bleeding</b> - bloody or tarry stools, coughing up blood or vomit that looks like coffee grounds;</p>
<b>signs of stomach bleeding</b>
<p><b>liver problems</b> - nausea, upper stomach pain, itching, tired feeling, flu-like symptoms, loss of appetite, dark urine, clay-colored stools, jaundice (yellowing of the skin or eyes);</p>
<b>liver problems</b>
<p><b>kidney problems</b> - little or no urinating, painful or difficult urination, swelling in your feet or ankles, feeling tired or short of breath;</p>
<b>kidney problems</b>
<p><b>low red blood cells (anemia)</b> - pale skin, feeling light-headed or short of breath, rapid heart rate, trouble concentrating; or</p>
<b>low red blood cells (anemia)</b>
<p><b>severe skin reaction</b> - fever, sore throat, swelling in your face or tongue, burning in your eyes, skin pain followed by a red or purple skin rash that spreads (especially in the face or upper body) and causes blistering and peeling.</p>
<b>severe skin reaction</b>
<p>Common Aleve side effects may include:</p>
<p>indigestion, heartburn, stomach pain, nausea;</p>
<p>headache, dizziness, drowsiness;</p>
<p>bruising, itching, rash;</p>
<p>swelling; or</p>
<p>ringing in your ears.</p>
<p>This is not a complete list of side effects and others may occur. Call your doctor for medical advice about side effects. You may report side effects to FDA at 1-800-FDA-1088.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="interactions">What other drugs will affect Aleve?</h2>
<p><b>Ask your doctor before using Aleve if you take an antidepressant</b> such as citalopram, escitalopram, fluoxetine (Prozac), fluvoxamine, paroxetine, sertraline (Zoloft), trazodone, or vilazodone. Taking any of these medicines with an NSAID may cause you to bruise or bleed easily.</p>
<b>Ask your doctor before using Aleve if you take an antidepressant</b>
<p>Ask a doctor or pharmacist if it is safe for you to use Aleve if you are also using any of the following drugs:</p>
<p>cholestyramine;</p>
<p>cyclosporine;</p>
<p>digoxin;</p>
<p>lithium;</p>
<p>methotrexate;</p>
<p>pemetrexed;</p>
<p>phenytoin or similar seizure medications;</p>
<p>probenecid;</p>
<p>warfarin (Coumadin, Jantoven) or similar blood thinners;</p>
<p>a diuretic or "water pill";</p>
<p>heart or blood pressure medication; or</p>
<p>insulin or oral diabetes medicine.</p>
<p>This list is not complete. Other drugs may interact with naproxen, including prescription and over-the-counter medicines, vitamins, and herbal products. Not all possible interactions are listed in this medication guide.</p>
