Allegra:
 <p>Generic Name:  (FEX oh FEN a deen)<br/>
Brand Names: <i>Allegra, Allegra ODT</i></p>
<p class="ddc-reviewed-by"><span>Medically reviewed by . Last updated on Jan 4, 2021.</span></p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is Allegra?</h2>
<p>Allegra (fexofenadine) is an antihistamine that reduces the effects of natural chemical histamine in the body. Histamine can produce symptoms of sneezing, itching, watery eyes, and runny nose.</p>
<p>Allegra is used to treat the symptoms of seasonal allergies (hay fever) in adults and children.</p>
<p>Allegra is also used to treat skin itching and hives caused by a condition called chronic idiopathic urticaria in adults and children.</p>
<p>Allegra may also be used for purposes not listed in this medication guide.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Ask a doctor or pharmacist before taking Allegra if you are allergic to any drugs, or if you have kidney disease.</p>
<p>Do not take Allegra with fruit juice (such as apple, orange, or grapefruit).</p>
<p>There may be other drugs that can affect Allegra. Tell your doctor about all medications you use. This includes prescription, over-the-counter, vitamin, and herbal products. Do not start a new medication without telling your doctor.</p>
<p>Stop using Allegra and get emergency medical help if you think you have used too much medicine, or if you have any of these signs of an allergic reaction: hives; difficulty breathing; swelling of your face, lips, tongue, or throat.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if your symptoms do not improve, or if they get worse after you start taking Allegra. Never use more than the recommended dose.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>Ask a doctor or pharmacist if it is safe for you to take Allegra if you are allergic to any drugs, or if you have kidney disease.</p>
<p>FDA pregnancy category C. It is not known whether Allegra will harm an unborn baby. Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or plan to become pregnant while using this medicine. It is not known whether fexofenadine passes into breast milk or if it could harm a nursing baby. Do not use this medication without telling your doctor if you are breast-feeding a baby. Allegra tablets and capsules may be used to treat seasonal allergy symptoms in children who are at least 6 years old. Allegra oral suspension (liquid) may be used in children ages 2 through 11. When treating chronic idiopathic urticaria, the liquid may be used in children as young as 2 months old. Do not give this medicine to a child without medical advice.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">How should I take Allegra?</h2>
<p>Use Allegra exactly as directed on the label, or as prescribed by your doctor. Do not use in larger or smaller amounts or for longer than recommended.</p>
<p>Take the regular tablet with a full glass of water. Do not use any other type of liquid. Shake the oral suspension (liquid) well just before you measure a dose. To be sure you get the correct dose, measure the liquid with a marked measuring spoon or medicine cup, not with a regular table spoon. If you do not have a dose-measuring device, ask your pharmacist for one.</p>
<p>To take fexofenadine orally disintegrating tablets (Allegra ODT):</p>
<p>Keep the tablet in its blister pack until you are ready to take the medicine. Open the package and peel back the foil from the tablet blister. Do not push a tablet through the foil or you may damage the tablet.</p>
<p>Using dry hands, remove the tablet and place it in your mouth. It will begin to dissolve right away.</p>
<p>Do not swallow the tablet whole. Allow it to dissolve in your mouth without chewing.</p>
<p>Swallow several times as the tablet dissolves. If desired, you may drink liquid to help swallow the dissolved tablet.</p>
<p>Take the Allegra disintegrating tablet on an empty stomach, at least 1 hour before or 2 hours after a meal.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if your symptoms do not improve, or if they get worse after you start taking Allegra. Never use more than the recommended dose.</p>
<p>Store Allegra at room temperature away from moisture and heat. Keep the medicine bottle tightly closed.</p>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Since cold or allergy medicine is taken as needed, you may not be on a dosing schedule. If you are taking the medication regularly, take the missed dose as soon as you remember. Skip the missed dose if it is almost time for your next scheduled dose. Do not take extra medicine to make up the missed dose.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222.</p>
<p>Overdose symptoms may include dry mouth, dizziness, or drowsiness.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What should I avoid?</h2>
<p>Avoid using antacids within 15 minutes before or after taking a medication that contains Allegra. Antacids can make it harder for your body to absorb this medication.</p>
<p>Fruit juices and certain antacids can make it harder for your body to absorb fexofenadine. Do not take Allegra with fruit juice (such as apple, orange, or grapefruit).</p>
<p>Avoid taking any other cold or allergy medicines unless your doctor has told you to.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="side-effects">Allegra side effects</h2>
<p>Get emergency medical help if you have any of these signs of an allergic reaction to Allegra: hives; difficulty breathing; swelling of your face, lips, tongue, or throat. Stop taking Allegra and call your doctor if you have fever, chills, body aches, cough, or other flu symptoms.</p>
<p>Less serious Allegra side effects may include:</p>
<p>nausea, diarrhea, upset stomach;</p>
<p>menstrual cramps;</p>
<p>drowsiness, tired feeling;</p>
<p>headache; or</p>
<p>muscle or back pain.</p>
<p>This is not a complete list of side effects and others may occur. Call your doctor for medical advice about side effects. You may report side effects to FDA at 1-800-FDA-1088.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="interactions">What other drugs will affect Allegra?</h2>
<p>Before taking this medication, tell your doctor if you regularly use other medicines that make you sleepy (such as cold or allergy medicine, sedatives, narcotic pain medicine, sleeping pills, muscle relaxers, and medicine for seizures, depression, or anxiety). They can add to sleepiness caused by Allegra.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor about all other medicines you use, especially:</p>
<p>ketoconazole (Nizoral); or</p>
<p>erythromycin (E.E.S., EryPed, Ery-Tab, Erythrocin, Pediazole).</p>
<p>This list is not complete and other drugs may interact with Allegra. Tell your doctor about all medications you use. This includes prescription, over-the-counter, vitamin, and herbal products. Do not start a new medication without telling your doctor.</p>

Allopurinol:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b> allopurinol (AL oh PURE i nol)<br/>
<b>Brand Name:</b> <i>Aloprim, Zyloprim, Lopurin</i><br/>
<b>Dosage Forms:</b> intravenous powder for injection (500 mg); oral tablet (100 mg; 300 mg)</p>
<b>Generic Name:</b>
<b>Brand Name:</b>
<b>Dosage Forms:</b>
<p class="ddc-reviewed-by"><span>Medically reviewed by . Last updated on March 5, 2021.</span></p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is allopurinol?</h2>
<p> reduces the production of uric acid in the body. Uric acid buildup can lead to gout or kidney stones.</p>
<p>Allopurinol is used to treat  or .</p>
<p>Allopurinol is also used to decrease levels of uric acid in people who are receiving cancer treatment.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Allopurinol can lower blood cells that help your body fight infections. This can make it easier for you to bleed from an injury or get sick from being around others who are ill. Your blood may need to be tested often. Visit your doctor regularly.</p>
<p>You should not use this medicine if you have ever had a serious allergic reaction to allopurinol. <b>Stop taking the medicine and call your doctor at once if you have any signs of skin rash (no matter how mild), painful urination, blood in your urine, burning in your eyes, or swelling in your face or throat.</b></p>
<b>Stop taking the medicine and call your doctor at once if you have any signs of skin rash (no matter how mild), painful urination, blood in your urine, burning in your eyes, or swelling in your face or throat.</b>
<p>Avoid drinking alcohol. It can make your condition worse. Allopurinol may impair your thinking or reactions. Be careful if you drive or do anything that requires you to be alert.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="side-effects">Allopurinol side effects</h2>
<p>Stop using this medicine and get emergency medical help if you have <b>signs of an allergic reaction to allopurinol</b> (, difficult breathing, swelling in your face or throat) <b>or a severe skin reaction</b> (fever, , burning eyes, skin pain, red or purple  with blistering and peeling).</p>
<b>signs of an allergic reaction to allopurinol</b>
<b>or a severe skin reaction</b>
<p><b>Seek medical treatment if you have a serious drug reaction that can affect many parts of your body.</b> Symptoms may include: skin rash, fever, swollen glands, muscle aches, severe weakness, unusual bruising, or yellowing of your skin or eyes.</p>
<b>Seek medical treatment if you have a serious drug reaction that can affect many parts of your body.</b>
<p>Stop using allopurinol and call your doctor at once if you have:</p>
<p>any skin rash, no matter how mild;</p>
<p>painful urination, blood in the urine;</p>
<p>little or no urination;</p>
<p>easy bruising, unusual bleeding;</p>
<p>, tingling, burning pain;</p>
<p>worsening gout symptoms; or</p>
<p><b>liver problems</b> - loss of appetite, , stomach pain (upper right side), itching, dark urine, clay-colored stools,  (yellowing of the skin or eyes).</p>
<b>liver problems</b>
<p>Common allopurinol side effects may include:</p>
<p>an increase in gout attacks when you first starting taking allopurinol oral;</p>
<p>rash;</p>
<p>drowsiness;</p>
<p>fever, chills;</p>
<p>abnormal ;</p>
<p>, ; or</p>
<p>joint pain.</p>
<p>This is not a complete list of side effects and others may occur. Call your doctor for medical advice about side effects. You may report side effects to FDA at 1-800-FDA-1088.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not use allopurinol if you are allergic to it.</p>
<p>To make sure allopurinol is safe for you, tell your doctor if you have ever had:</p>
<p>kidney disease;</p>
<p>;</p>
<p>diabetes;</p>
<p>congestive ;</p>
<p>;</p>
<p>if you are receiving ; or</p>
<p>if you have a gene variation called HLA-B*58:01 allele (your doctor will test you for this).</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or breastfeeding.</p>
<p>Do not give this medicine to a child without medical advice.</p>
<h2>How should I use allopurinol?</h2>
<p>Take allopurinol exactly as prescribed by your doctor. Follow all directions on your prescription label and read all medication guides or instruction sheets. Your doctor may occasionally change your dose.</p>
<p>Take allopurinol <b>oral</b> with a full glass of water. To reduce your risk of kidney stones forming, drink 8 to 10 full glasses of fluid every day, unless your doctor tells you otherwise.</p>
<b>oral</b>
<p>If this medicine upsets your stomach, take allopurinol <b>oral</b> after a meal.</p>
<b>oral</b>
<p>Allopurinol injection is given as an infusion into a vein if you are unable to take the medicine by mouth. A healthcare provider will give your first dose and may teach you how to properly use the medication by yourself.</p>
<p>You may need to mix the injection with a liquid (diluent) in an IV bag. When using injections by yourself, be sure you understand how to properly mix and store the medicine. Ask your doctor or pharmacist if you don't understand all instructions.</p>
<p>Prepare an injection only when you are ready to give it. Do not use if the medicine has changed colors or has particles in it. Call your pharmacist for new medicine.</p>
<p>You may need frequent medical tests. Even if you have no symptoms, tests can help your doctor determine if allopurinol is effective.</p>
<p>You may have gout attacks more often when you first start taking this medicine oral. Your doctor may recommend other gout medication to take with allopurinol. Keep taking the medicine as directed.</p>
<p><b>It may take 2 to 6 weeks before you have fewer gout attacks.</b> Call your doctor if your symptoms do not improve after 6 weeks.</p>
<b>It may take 2 to 6 weeks before you have fewer gout attacks.</b>
<p>You may need to follow a special diet to help prevent kidney stones. Follow all instructions of your doctor or dietitian. Learn about the foods to eat or avoid.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture and heat.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">Dosing information</h2>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose of Allopurinol for Gout:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose of Allopurinol for Gout:</b>
<p>Dose will vary with the severity of the disease:<br/>
<br/>
Initial dose: 100 mg orally once a day<br/>
-Increase in increments of 100 mg weekly until a serum uric level of 6 mg/dL or less is attained<br/>
<br/>
Mild Gout:<br/>
-Average maintenance dose: 200 to 300 mg orally once a day<br/>
Moderately Severe Tophaceous Gout:<br/>
-Average maintenance dose: 400 to 600 mg orally/day in divided doses<br/>
Minimal Effective Dose: 100 to 200 mg per day<br/>
Maximum Dose: 800 mg per day<br/>
<br/>
Comments:<br/>
-Oral doses in excess of 300 mg/day should be given in divided doses, preferably after meals to minimize gastric irritation.<br/>
-A gradual dose titration is recommended to reduce the possibility of acute gouty attacks.<br/>
-Normal serum urate levels are usually achieved in 1 to 3 weeks.<br/>
<br/>
Use: For the management of patients with signs and symptoms of primary or secondary gout (acute attacks, tophi, joint destruction, uric acid lithiasis, and/or nephropathy).</p>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose of Allopurinol for Hyperuricemia Secondary to Chemotherapy:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose of Allopurinol for Hyperuricemia Secondary to Chemotherapy:</b>
<p>Parenteral:<br/>
200 to 400 mg/m2/day IV as a single infusion or in equally divided infusions at 6, 8, or 12 hour intervals<br/>
Maximum dose: 600 mg/day<br/>
<br/>
Oral:<br/>
Initial dose: 600 to 800 mg orally in divided doses<br/>
Maintenance: Adjust dose as needed based on serum uric acid levels<br/>
Maximum dose: 800 mg per day<br/>
<br/>
Comments:<br/>
-When possible, therapy should be initiated 24 to 48 hours before the start of chemotherapy; treatment should be discontinued when the potential for overproduction of uric acid is no longer present.<br/>
-Oral doses in excess of 300 mg/day should be given in divided doses, preferably after meals to minimize gastric irritation.<br/>
-The dose to lower serum uric acid to normal or near-normal varies with the severity of the disease; the above dosing represents suggested doses; serum uric acid levels should serve as an index.<br/>
-Fluid intake should be sufficient to maintain a daily urinary output of at least 2 L; neutral or preferably slightly alkaline urine is desirable.<br/>
<br/>
Use: For the management of patients with leukemia, lymphoma, and malignancies who are receiving cancer therapy which causes elevations of serum and urinary uric acid levels; IV therapy is available for patients who cannot tolerate oral therapy.</p>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose of Allopurinol for Calcium Oxalate Calculi with Hyperuricosuria:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose of Allopurinol for Calcium Oxalate Calculi with Hyperuricosuria:</b>
<p>200 to 300 mg orally once a day or in divided doses<br/>
<br/>
Comments:<br/>
-Carefully assess risk versus benefit when initiating therapy and periodically thereafter.<br/>
-Dose adjustments should be based on control of hyperuricosuria based on 24-hour urinary urate determinations.<br/>
-Clinical experience suggests these patients may benefit dietary changes in addition to drug therapy.<br/>
<br/>
Use: For the management recurrent calcium oxalate calculi in patients whose daily uric acid excretion exceeds 800 mg/day in males or 750 mg/day in females.</p>
<p><b>Usual Pediatric Dose for Hyperuricemia Secondary to Chemotherapy:</b></p>
<b>Usual Pediatric Dose for Hyperuricemia Secondary to Chemotherapy:</b>
<p>Parenteral:<br/>
Initial dose: 200 mg/m2/day IV as a single infusion or in equally divided infusions at 6, 8, or 12 hour intervals<br/>
Maximum dose: 600 mg/day<br/>
<br/>
Oral:<br/>
Age: Less than 6 years: 150 mg orally once a day or in divided doses<br/>
Age: 6 to 10 years: 300 mg orally once a day or in divided doses<br/>
Age: Greater than 10 years: 600 to 800 mg orally per day in divided doses<br/>
-After 48 hours, evaluate and adjust dose as needed<br/>
<br/>
Comments:<br/>
-Oral doses in excess of 300 mg should be administered in divided doses.<br/>
-When possible, therapy should be initiated 24 to 48 hours before the start of chemotherapy; treatment should be discontinued when the potential for overproduction of uric acid is no longer present.<br/>
-The dose to lower serum uric acid to normal or near-normal varies with the severity of the disease; the above dosing represents suggested doses in children; serum uric acid levels should serve as an index.<br/>
-Fluid intake should be sufficient to maintain a daily urinary output of at least 2 L; neutral or preferably slightly alkaline urine is desirable.<br/>
<br/>
Use: For the management of patients with leukemia, lymphoma, and malignancies who are receiving cancer therapy which causes elevations of serum and urinary uric acid levels.</p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p><b>Alprazolam can slow or stop your breathing, especially if you have recently used an opioid medication, alcohol, or other drugs that can slow your breathing.</b></p>
<b>Alprazolam can slow or stop your breathing, especially if you have recently used an opioid medication, alcohol, or other drugs that can slow your breathing.</b>
<p>You should not use alprazolam if you have narrow-angle glaucoma, if you also take itraconazole or ketoconazole, or if you are allergic to alprazolam or similar medicines (Valium, Ativan, Tranxene, and others).</p>
<p><b>Do not use alprazolam if you are pregnant.</b> This medicine can cause birth defects or life-threatening withdrawal symptoms in a newborn.</p>
<b>Do not use alprazolam if you are pregnant.</b>
<p>Alprazolam may be habit-forming and should be used only by the person for whom it was prescribed. Keep the medication in a secure place where others cannot get to it. <b>Misuse can cause addiction, overdose, or death.</b></p>
<b>Misuse can cause addiction, overdose, or death.</b>
<p><b>Fatal side effects can occur if you take alprazolam with alcohol, opioid medicine, or other drugs that cause drowsiness or slow your breathing.</b></p>
<b>Fatal side effects can occur if you take alprazolam with alcohol, opioid medicine, or other drugs that cause drowsiness or slow your breathing.</b>

<b>Avoid taking this medicine during the first trimester of pregnancy.</b>
<p><b>If you use alprazolam while you are pregnant, your baby could become dependent on the drug.</b> This can cause life-threatening withdrawal symptoms in the baby after it is born. Babies born dependent on habit-forming medicine may need medical treatment for several weeks.</p>

-Maximum dose: 10 mg/day<br/>
<br/>
Comments:<br/>
-The lowest possible effective dose should be administered and the need for continued treatment reassessed frequently.<br/>
-Dosage should be reduced gradually when discontinuing therapy or when decreasing the daily dosage.<br/>
-The daily dosage may be decreased by no more than 0.5 mg every 3 days; however, some patients may require an even slower dosage reduction.<br/>
-The dose of extended-release tablets may be increased at intervals of 3 to 4 days in increments of no more than 1 mg per day.<br/>
-The times of administration should be distributed as evenly as possible throughout the waking hours.</p>

Amantadine:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b> amantadine (a MAN ta deen)<br/>
<b>Brand Name:</b> <i>Gocovri, Osmolex ER, Symmetrel</i></p>
<b>Generic Name:</b>
<b>Brand Name:</b>
<p class="ddc-reviewed-by"><span>Medically reviewed by . Last updated on Nov 5, 2020.</span></p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is amantadine?</h2>
<p> is an antiviral medicine that blocks the actions of viruses in your body.</p>
<p>Amantadine is used to treat  and "Parkinson-like" symptoms such as stiffness or tremors, shaking, and repetitive uncontrolled muscle movements that may be caused by the use of certain drugs.</p>
<p>Amantadine is also used to treat or prevent  in adults and children. It may not be effective during every flu season because certain strains of the virus may be resistant to amantadine. This medicine should not be used in place of getting a yearly flu shot. The Centers for Disease Control recommends an annual flu shot to help protect you each year from new strains of  virus.</p>
<p>Amantadine is available as tablets, capsules, and oral solution.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>You should not use amantadine if you received a nasal flu vaccine in the past 14 days.</p>
<p>Do not receive a nasal flu vaccine while taking amantadine, and for at least 48 hours after your last dose. You may receive a flu shot (injection) while taking amantadine.</p>
<p>Avoid driving and doing other tasks or actions that call for you to be alert or have clear eyesight until you see how this amantadine affects you.</p>
<p>To lower the chance of feeling dizzy or passing out, rise slowly if you have been sitting or lying down. Be careful going up and down stairs.</p>
<p>Heat stroke has happened in people taking amantadine. Be careful in hot weather and during physical activity.</p>
<p>If you have kidney problems, talk with your doctor. Your dose may need to be changed based on how well your kidneys work. Deaths have happened in people with kidney problems whose dose was too high for their kidney function.</p>
<p>Do not stop taking amantadine all of a sudden without calling your doctor. You may have a greater risk of side effects. If you need to stop amantadine, you will want to slowly stop it as ordered by your doctor.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not use amantadine if you are allergic to it, or if:</p>
<p>you have severe kidney disease; or</p>
<p>you received a "live" nasal flu vaccine (FluMist) within the past 14 days.</p>
<p>To make sure amantadine is safe for you, tell your doctor if you have ever had:</p>
<p>kidney disease;</p>
<p>daytime drowsiness (caused by a sleep disorder or taking certain medicines);</p>
<p>congestive heart failure;</p>
<p>eczema;</p>
<p>glaucoma;</p>
<p>liver disease;</p>
<p>a seizure;</p>
<p>low blood pressure, fainting spells;</p>
<p> or ; or</p>
<p>mental illness, psychosis, or suicidal thoughts or actions.</p>
<p>People with Parkinson's disease may have a higher risk of skin cancer (melanoma). Talk to your doctor about this risk and what skin symptoms to watch for.</p>
<p>It is not known whether amantadine will harm an unborn baby. Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or plan to become pregnant.</p>
<p>You should not breast-feed while using this medicine.</p>
<p>Amantadine is not approved for influenza in a child younger than 1 year old. <b>Gocovri</b> is not approved for use by anyone younger than 18 years old.</p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="faq">Popular FAQ</h2>
<p>The main differences between Gocovri and Osmolex ER center around their approved uses, dosage forms, strength and study designs for FDA approval. Approval of Gocovri was based on placebo-controlled clinical studies in patients with Parkinson's disease with levodopa-induced dyskinesias, whereas the effectiveness of Osmolex ER was based upon bioavailability studies that compared Osmolex ER to immediate-release amantadine. Gocovri and Osmolex ER are not interchangeable with other amantadine immediate- or extended-release products. </p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is Ambien?</h2>
<p>Ambien () is a sedative, also called a hypnotic. Zolpidem affects chemicals in the brain that may be unbalanced in people with sleep problems insomnia).</p>
<p>Ambien is used to treat . The immediate-release tablet is used to help you fall asleep when you first go to bed. The extended-release form, Ambien CR, which has a first layer that dissolves quickly to help you fall asleep, and a second layer that dissolves slowly to help you stay asleep.</p>
<p>Your doctor will determine which form of Ambien is best for you.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>

<p>Ambien may impair your thinking or reactions. You may still feel sleepy the morning after taking this medicine, especially if you take the extended-release tablet, or if you are a woman. Wait at least 4 hours or until you are fully awake before you do anything that requires you to be awake and alert.</p>

<p>You should not use Ambien if you are allergic to zolpidem. The tablets may contain lactose. Use caution if you are sensitive to lactose.</p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is amiodarone?</h2>
<p> affects the . It is used to help keep the heart beating normally in people with life-threatening heart rhythm disorders of the ventricles (the lower chambers of the heart that allow blood to flow out of the heart).</p>
<p>Amiodarone is used to treat  or .</p>
<p>Amiodarone is for use only in treating life-threatening heart rhythm disorders.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Amiodarone can cause dangerous side effects on your heart, liver, lungs, or vision.</p>
<p>You should not take this medicine if you are allergic to amiodarone or , or if you have , a history of slow heartbeats that have caused you to faint, or if your heart cannot pump blood properly.</p>
<p>Call your doctor or get medical help at once if you have: chest pain, fast or pounding heartbeats, trouble breathing, vision problems, upper stomach pain, , dark urine,  (yellowing of the skin or eyes), or if you cough up blood.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if you have signs of a thyroid problem, such as weight changes, extreme tiredness, dry skin, thinning hair, feeling too hot or too cold, irregular menstrual periods, or swelling in your neck (goiter).</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not use amiodarone if you have:</p>
<p>a serious heart condition called "AV block" (2nd or 3rd degree), unless you have a ;</p>
<p>a history of slow heartbeats that have caused you to faint; or</p>
<p>if your heart cannot pump blood properly.</p>
<p>Amiodarone can cause dangerous side effects on your heart, liver, lungs, or thyroid.</p>

<p> or another lung disorder;</p>
<p>;</p>
<p>a thyroid disorder;</p>
<p>vision problems;</p>
<p>high or ;</p>
<p>an electrolyte imbalance (such as low levels of potassium or magnesium in your blood); or</p>
<p>if you have a pacemaker or defibrillator implanted in your chest.</p>
<p><b>Taking amiodarone during pregnancy may harm an unborn baby,</b> or cause thyroid problems or abnormal heartbeats in the baby after it is born. Amiodarone may also affect the child's growth or development (speech, movement, academic skills) later in life. Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or if you become pregnant.</p>
<b>Taking amiodarone during pregnancy may harm an unborn baby,</b>
<p>You should not breast-feed while taking this medicine, and for several months after stopping. <b>Amiodarone takes a long time to clear from your body.</b> Talk to your doctor about the best way to feed your baby during this time.</p>
<b>Amiodarone takes a long time to clear from your body.</b>
<h2>How should I take amiodarone?</h2>
<p>Take amiodarone exactly as prescribed by your doctor. Follow all directions on your prescription label and read all medication guides or instruction sheets. Your doctor may occasionally change your dose.</p>
<p>You will receive your first few doses in a hospital setting, where your heart rhythm can be monitored.</p>
<p>If you have been taking another heart rhythm medicine, you may need to gradually stop taking it when you start using amiodarone. Follow your doctor's dosing instructions very carefully.</p>
<p>You may take the tablets with or without food, but take it the same way each time.</p>
<p>It may take up to 3 weeks before your heart rhythm improves. Keep using the medicine as directed even if you feel well.</p>
<p>Amiodarone can have long lasting effects on your body. You may need frequent medical tests while using this medicine and for several months after your last dose.</p>
<p>If you need surgery (including laser eye surgery), tell the surgeon ahead of time that you are using amiodarone.</p>
<p>This medicine can affect the results of certain medical tests. Tell any doctor who treats you that you are using this medicine.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture, heat, and light.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">Dosing information</h2>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose for Arrhythmias:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose for Arrhythmias:</b>
<p>IV:<br/>
Initial dose: 1000 mg over the first 24 hours of therapy, delivered by the following infusion regimen:<br/>
-Loading infusions: 150 mg over the first 10 minutes (15 mg/min), followed by 360 mg over the next 6 hours (1 mg/min)<br/>
-Maintenance infusion: 540 mg over the remaining 18 hours (0.5 mg/min)<br/>
<br/>
Maintenance dose: After the first 24 hours, continue the maintenance infusion rate of 0.5 mg/min; may increase infusion rate to achieve effective arrhythmia suppression.<br/>
-Supplemental infusions: 150 mg over 10 minutes (15 mg/min) for breakthrough episodes of ventricular fibrillation (VF) or hemodynamically unstable ventricular tachycardia (VT)<br/>
<br/>
Maximum dose: Initial infusion rate: 30 mg/min<br/>
<br/>
Duration of therapy: Until ventricular arrhythmias stabilize (most patients require 48 to 96 hours); maintenance infusion of up to 0.5 mg/min can be continued for up to 3 weeks.<br/>
<br/>
Comments: Mean daily doses greater than 2100 mg for the first 24 hours were associated with increased risk of hypotension.<br/>
<br/>
Use: Initiation of treatment and prophylaxis of frequently recurring VF and hemodynamically unstable VT in patients refractory to other therapy.<br/>
<br/>
<br/>
ORAL:<br/>
Loading dose: 800 to 1600 mg orally per day for 1 to 3 weeks (occasionally longer) until adequate arrhythmia control is achieved or if side effects become prominent, then switch to adjustment dose<br/>
Adjustment dose: 600 to 800 mg orally per day for 1 month, then switch to maintenance dose<br/>
Maintenance dose: 400 mg orally per day<br/>
<br/>
Comments:<br/>
-May be administered once a day; twice a day dosing is recommended for total daily doses of 1000 mg or more or in patients who experience gastrointestinal tolerance.<br/>
-Close monitoring is indicated during the loading phase and surrounding any dose adjustments.<br/>
-Maintenance dose should be determined according to antiarrhythmic effect as assessed by patient tolerance as well as symptoms, Holter recordings, and/or programmed electrical stimulation; some patients may require up to 600 mg/day while some can be controlled on lower doses.<br/>
<br/>
Use: Treatment of life-threatening recurrent VF or life-threatening recurrent hemodynamically unstable VT in patients refractory to adequate doses of other antiarrhythmics or those intolerant of alternative agents.</p>

<p>Many drugs can interact with amiodarone. This includes prescription and over-the-counter medicines, , and . Not all possible interactions are listed here. Tell your doctor about all your current medicines and any medicine you start or stop using.</p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is amitriptyline?</h2>
<p> is a tricyclic  with sedative effects. Amitriptyline affects certain chemical messengers (neurotransmitters) that communicate between brain cells and help regulate mood.</p>
<p>Amitriptyline is a prescription medicine used to treat symptoms of .</p>
<p>Amitriptyline may also be used for purposes not listed in this medication guide.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>You should not use amitriptyline if you have recently had a .</p>
<p>Do not use amitriptyline if you have used an  in the past 14 days, such as , ,  injection, , , , or .</p>
<p>You may have thoughts about suicide when you first start taking an antidepressant such as amitriptyline, especially if you are younger than 24 years old. Your doctor will need to check you at regular visits for at least the first 12 weeks of treatment.</p>
<p>Report any new or worsening symptoms to your doctor, such as: mood or behavior changes, anxiety, panic attacks, trouble sleeping, or if you feel impulsive, irritable, agitated, hostile, aggressive, restless, hyperactive (mentally or physically), more depressed, or have thoughts about suicide or hurting yourself.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not use this medicine if you are allergic to amitriptyline, or:</p>
<p>if you have recently had a heart attack.</p>
<p>Do not use amitriptyline if you have used an MAO inhibitor in the past 14 days. A dangerous drug interaction could occur. MAO inhibitors include isocarboxazid, linezolid, methylene blue injection, phenelzine, rasagiline, selegiline, tranylcypromine, and others.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if you have used an "SSRI" antidepressant in the past 5 weeks, such as , ,  (), , ,  (), , or .</p>

<p>diabetes (amitriptyline may raise or lower blood sugar);</p>
<p>; or</p>
<p>problems with urination.</p>
<p>Some young people have thoughts about suicide when first taking an antidepressant. Your doctor should check your progress at regular visits. Your family or other caregivers should also be alert to changes in your mood or symptoms.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or breastfeeding.</p>
<p>Amitriptyline is not approved for use by anyone younger than 12 years old.</p>
<h2>How should I take amitriptyline?</h2>
<p>Take amitriptyline exactly as prescribed by your doctor. Follow all directions on your prescription label and read all medication guides or instruction sheets. Your doctor may occasionally change your dose.</p>
<p>It may take up to 4 weeks before your symptoms improve. Keep using the medication as directed and tell your doctor if your symptoms do not improve.</p>
<p>If you need surgery, tell your surgeon you currently use amitriptyline. You may need to stop for a short time.</p>
<p>Do not stop using amitriptyline suddenly, or you could have unpleasant withdrawal symptoms. Ask your doctor how to safely stop using amitriptyline.</p>

-The full therapeutic effect may take as long as 30 days to develop.<br/>
-Maintenance doses should be reduced to the lowest amount that will maintain relief of symptoms when satisfactory improvement has been obtained.<br/>
-Maintenance therapy should be continued for 3 months or longer to lessen the possibility of relapse.<br/>

Amlodipine:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b> amlodipine (am LOE di peen)<br/>
<b>Brand Name:</b> <i>Katerzia, Norvasc</i></p>
<b>Generic Name:</b>
<b>Brand Name:</b>
<p class="ddc-reviewed-by"><span>Medically reviewed by . Last updated on Dec 1, 2019.</span></p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is amlodipine?</h2>
<p>Amlodipine is a calcium channel blocker that dilates (widens) blood vessels and improves blood flow.</p>
<p>Amlodipine is used to treat chest pain  and other conditions caused by .</p>
<p>Amlodipine is also used to treat  (hypertension). Lowering blood pressure may lower your risk of a stroke or heart attack.</p>
<p>Amlodipine is for use in adults and children who are at least 6 years old.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Before taking amlodipine, tell your doctor if you have congestive heart failure or liver disease.</p>
<p>Drinking alcohol can further lower your blood pressure and may increase certain side effects of amlodipine.</p>
<p>If you are being treated for high blood pressure, keep using amlodipine even if you feel well. High blood pressure often has no symptoms. You may need to use blood pressure medication for the rest of your life.</p>
<p>Amlodipine is only part of a complete program of treatment that may also include diet, exercise, weight control, and other medications. Follow your diet, medication, and exercise routines very closely.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor about all other heart or blood pressure medications you are taking.</p>
<p>Your chest pain may become worse when you first start taking amlodipine or when your dose is increased. Call your doctor if your chest pain is severe or ongoing.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not take amlodipine if you are allergic to it.</p>
<p>To make sure amlodipine is safe for you, tell your doctor if you have ever had:</p>
<p>liver disease; or</p>
<p>a heart valve problem called aortic stenosis.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or plan to become pregnant. It is not known whether amlodipine will harm an unborn baby. However, having high blood pressure during pregnancy may cause complications such as diabetes or eclampsia (dangerously high blood pressure that can lead to medical problems in both mother and baby). The benefit of treating hypertension may outweigh any risks to the baby.</p>
<p>Amlodipine can pass into breast milk, but effects on the nursing baby are not known. Tell your doctor if you are breast-feeding.</p>
<p>Amlodipine is not approved for use by anyone younger than 6 years old.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">How should I take amlodipine?</h2>
<p>Take amlodipine exactly as prescribed by your doctor. Follow all directions on your prescription label. Your doctor may occasionally change your dose to make sure you get the best results. Do not use this medicine in larger or smaller amounts or for longer than recommended.</p>
<p>You may take amlodipine with or without food. Take the medicine at the same time each day.</p>
<p>Shake the <b>Katerzia oral suspension</b> (liquid) before you measure a dose. Use the dosing syringe provided, or use a medicine dose-measuring device (not a kitchen spoon).</p>
<b>Katerzia oral suspension</b>
<p>Your blood pressure will need to be checked often.</p>
<p>Your chest pain may become worse when you first start taking amlodipine or when your dose is increased. Call your doctor if your chest pain is severe or ongoing.</p>
<p>If you are being treated for high blood pressure, keep using amlodipine even if you feel well. High blood pressure often has no symptoms. You may need to use blood pressure medicine for the rest of your life.</p>
<p>Your hypertension or heart condition may be treated with a combination of drugs. Use all medications as directed by your doctor. Read the medication guide or patient instructions provided with each medication. Do not change your doses or stop taking any of your medications without your doctor's advice. This is especially important if you also take nitroglycerin.</p>
<p>Amlodipine is only part of a complete program of treatment that may also include diet, exercise, weight control, and other medications. Follow your diet, medication, and exercise routines very closely.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture, heat, and light.</p>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Take the missed dose as soon as you remember. If you are more than 12 hours late, skip the missed dose. Do not take extra medicine to make up the missed dose.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222.</p>
<p>Overdose symptoms may include rapid heartbeats, redness or warmth in your arms or legs, or fainting.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What to avoid</h2>
<p>Avoid getting up too fast from a sitting or lying position, or you may feel dizzy. Get up slowly and steady yourself to prevent a fall.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="side-effects">Amlodipine side effects</h2>
<p>Get emergency medical help if you have <b>signs of an allergic reaction to amlodipine:</b> hives; difficulty breathing; swelling of your face, lips, tongue, or throat.</p>
<b>signs of an allergic reaction to amlodipine:</b>
<p>In rare cases, when you first start taking amlodipine, your angina may get worse or you could have a heart attack. <b>Seek emergency medical attention or call your doctor right away if you have symptoms such as:</b> chest pain or pressure, pain spreading to your jaw or shoulder, nausea, sweating.</p>
<b>Seek emergency medical attention or call your doctor right away if you have symptoms such as:</b>
<p>Call your doctor at once if you have:</p>
<p>pounding heartbeats or fluttering in your chest;</p>
<p>worsening chest pain;</p>
<p>swelling in your feet or ankles;</p>
<p>severe drowsiness; or</p>
<p>a light-headed feeling, like you might pass out.</p>
<p>Common amlodipine side effects may include:</p>
<p>dizziness, drowsiness;</p>
<p>feeling tired;</p>
<p>stomach pain, nausea; or</p>
<p>flushing (warmth, redness, or tingly feeling).</p>
<p>This is not a complete list of side effects and others may occur. Call your doctor for medical advice about side effects. You may report side effects to FDA at 1-800-FDA-1088.</p>

Amoxicillin:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b> amoxicillin (am OX i sil in)<br/>
<b>Brand Name:</b> <i>Amoxil, Trimox, Moxatag</i></p>
<b>Generic Name:</b>
<b>Brand Name:</b>
<p class="ddc-reviewed-by"><span>Medically reviewed by . Last updated on Jan 12, 2020.</span></p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is amoxicillin?</h2>
<p> is a penicillin antibiotic that fights bacteria.</p>
<p>Amoxicillin is used to treat many different types of infection caused by bacteria, such as tonsillitis, bronchitis, , and infections of the ear, nose, throat, skin, or urinary tract.</p>
<p>Amoxicillin is also sometimes used together with another antibiotic called  () to treat stomach ulcers caused by . This combination is sometimes used with a stomach acid reducer called  ().</p>
<b>There are many brands and forms of amoxicillin available and not all brands are listed on this leaflet.</b>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Do not use this medication if you are allergic to amoxicillin or to any other penicillin antibiotic, such as ampicillin (Omnipen, Principen), dicloxacillin (Dycill, Dynapen), oxacillin (Bactocill), penicillin (Beepen-VK, Ledercillin VK, Pen-V, Pen-Vee K, Pfizerpen, V-Cillin K, Veetids), and others.</p>
<p>Before using amoxicillin, tell your doctor if you are allergic to cephalosporins such as Omnicef, Cefzil, Ceftin, Keflex, and others. Also tell your doctor if you have asthma, liver or kidney disease, a bleeding or blood clotting disorder, mononucleosis (also called "mono"), or any type of allergy.</p>
<p>Amoxicillin can make birth control pills less effective. Ask your doctor about using a non-hormone method of birth control (such as a condom, diaphragm, spermicide) to prevent pregnancy while taking this medicine. Take this medication for the full prescribed length of time. Your symptoms may improve before the infection is completely cleared. Amoxicillin will not treat a viral infection such as the common cold or flu. Do not share this medication with another person, even if they have the same symptoms you have.</p>
<p>Antibiotic medicines can cause diarrhea. This may happen while you are taking amoxicillin, or within a few months after you stop taking it. This may be a sign of a new infection. If you have diarrhea that is watery or bloody, stop taking this medicine and call your doctor. Do not use anti-diarrhea medicine unless your doctor tells you to.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not use amoxicillin if you are allergic to any penicillin antibiotic, such as , , , penicillin, or ticarcillin.</p>

<p>There are several antibiotics that kill the common mouth bacteria that cause tooth infections. The best (first-line) antibiotics for tooth infection include: Amoxicillin, Penicillin, Cephalexin, Clindamycin, Azithromycin. Amoxicillin is often the first choice because it is widely effective and has the fewest gastrointestinal side effects. </p>

Amoxicillin and Clavulanate:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b> amoxicillin and clavulanate potassium (am OK i SIL in KLAV ue LAN ate poe TAS ee um)<br/>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is amoxicillin and clavulanate potassium?</h2>
<p> is a combination prescription antibiotic. Amoxicillin is a  that fights bacteria in the body. Clavulanate potassium is a beta-lactamase inhibitor that helps prevent certain bacteria from becoming resistant to amoxicillin.</p>
<p>Amoxicillin and clavulanate potassium is used to treat many different infections caused by bacteria, such as , , ear infections, , , and infections of the skin.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>You should not use amoxicillin and clavulanate potassium if you have severe kidney disease, if you have had liver problems or jaundice while taking this medicine previously, or if you are allergic to any penicillin or cephalosporin antibiotic, such as Amoxil, Ceftin, Cefzil, Levaquin, Moxatag, Omnicef, and others.</p>
<p>If you switch from one tablet form to another (regular, chewable, or extended-release tablet), take only the new tablet form and strength prescribed for you. Amoxicillin and clavulanate may not be as effective or could be harmful if you do not use the exact tablet form your doctor has prescribed.</p>
<p>Amoxicillin and clavulanate potassium can pass into breast milk and may harm a nursing baby. Do not use this medication without telling your doctor if you are breast-feeding a baby.</p>
<p>Amoxicillin and clavulanate potassium can make birth control pills less effective. Ask your doctor about using a non-hormone method of birth control (such as a condom, diaphragm, spermicide) to prevent pregnancy while taking this medicine.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not use this medicine if you are allergic to amoxicillin and clavulanate, or if:</p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is anastrozole?</h2>
<p>Anastrozole lowers estrogen levels in postmenopausal women, which may slow the growth of certain types of breast tumors that need estrogen to grow in the body.</p>
<p>Anastrozole is used to treat  in postmenopausal women. It is often given to women whose cancer has progressed even after taking  (Nolvadex, Soltamox).</p>
<p>Anastrozole may also be used for purposes not listed in this medication guide.</p>

<p>Apixaban is also used after hip or knee replacement surgery to prevent a type of blood clot called  (), which can lead to  in the lungs ().</p>
<p>Apixaban is also used to treat DVT or pulmonary embolism (PE), and to lower your risk of having a repeat DVT or PE.</p>
<p>Apixaban may also be used for purposes not listed in this medication guide.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p><b>Apixaban increases your risk of severe or fatal bleeding,</b> especially if you take certain medicines at the same time (including some over-the-counter medicines). <b>It is very important to tell your doctor about all medicines you have recently used.</b></p>
<b>Apixaban increases your risk of severe or fatal bleeding,</b>
<b>It is very important to tell your doctor about all medicines you have recently used.</b>
<p><b>Call your doctor at once if you have signs of bleeding such as:</b> swelling, pain, feeling very weak or dizzy, bleeding gums, , heavy menstrual periods or abnormal , blood in your urine, bloody or tarry stools,  or vomit that looks like coffee grounds, or any bleeding that will not stop.</p>
<b>Call your doctor at once if you have signs of bleeding such as:</b>
<p>Apixaban can cause a very serious blood clot around your spinal cord if you undergo a spinal tap or receive spinal anesthesia (epidural), especially if you have a genetic spinal defect, if you have a spinal catheter in place, if you have a history of spinal surgery or repeated spinal taps, or if you are also using other drugs that can affect blood clotting. This type of blood clot can lead to long-term or permanent paralysis.</p>

<p><b>Do not stop taking apixaban unless your doctor tells you to. Stopping suddenly can increase your risk of blood clot or stroke.</b></p>

<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not take apixaban if you are allergic to it, or if you have active bleeding from a surgery, injury, or other cause.</p>
<p>Apixaban may cause you to bleed more easily, especially if you have a bleeding disorder that is inherited or caused by disease.</p>
<p>Tell your doctor if you have an artificial heart valve, or if you have ever had:</p>
<p>liver or kidney disease;</p>
<p>if you are older than 80; or</p>
<p>if you weigh less than 132 pounds (60 kilograms).</p>
<p><b>Apixaban can cause a very serious blood clot around your spinal cord if you undergo a spinal tap or receive spinal anesthesia (epidural). This type of blood clot could cause long-term paralysis, and may be more likely to occur if:</b></p>
<b>Apixaban can cause a very serious blood clot around your spinal cord if you undergo a spinal tap or receive spinal anesthesia (epidural). This type of blood clot could cause long-term paralysis, and may be more likely to occur if:</b>

<p>You should not breast-feed while using  apixaban.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">How should I take apixaban?</h2>
<p>Follow all directions on your prescription label and read all medication guides or instruction sheets. Your doctor may occasionally change your dose. Use the medicine exactly as directed.</p>
<p>You may take apixaban with or without food.</p>
<p>If you cannot swallow a tablet whole, crush and mix it with water, apple juice, or a spoonful of applesauce. Swallow the mixture right away without chewing. Do not save it for later use.</p>
<p>A crushed tablet mixture may also be given through a nasogastric (NG) feeding tube. Read and carefully follow any Instructions for Use provided with your medicine. Ask your doctor or pharmacist if you do not understand these instructions.</p>
<p><b>Apixaban can make it easier for you to bleed, even from a minor injury.</b> Seek medical attention if you have bleeding that will not stop.</p>
<b>Apixaban can make it easier for you to bleed, even from a minor injury.</b>
<p>If you need surgery or dental work, tell the doctor or dentist ahead of time if you have taken apixaban within the past 24 hours. You may need to stop taking apixaban for a short time.</p>
<p>Do not stop taking apixaban unless your doctor tells you to. <b>Stopping suddenly can increase your risk of blood clot or stroke.</b></p>
<b>Stopping suddenly can increase your risk of blood clot or stroke.</b>
<p>If you stop taking apixaban for any reason, your doctor may prescribe another medication to prevent blood clots until you start taking apixaban again.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture and heat.</p>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Take the missed dose on the same day you remember it. Take your next dose at the regular time and stay on your twice-daily schedule. Do not take two doses at one time.</p>
<p>Get your prescription refilled before you run out of medicine completely.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What should I avoid while taking apixaban?</h2>
<p>Avoid activities that may increase your risk of bleeding or injury. Use extra care to prevent bleeding while shaving or brushing your teeth.</p>

Aricept:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b>  (oral) (doe NEP e zil)<br/>
<b>Brand Name:</b> <i>Aricept, Aricept ODT</i></p>
<b>Generic Name:</b>
<b>Brand Name:</b>
<p class="ddc-reviewed-by"><span>Medically reviewed by . Last updated on Feb 1, 2021.</span></p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is Aricept?</h2>
<p>Aricept (donepezil) improves the function of nerve cells in the brain. It works by preventing the breakdown of a chemical called acetylcholine (ah SEET il KOE leen). People with dementia usually have lower levels of this chemical, which is important for the processes of memory, thinking, and reasoning.</p>
<p>Aricept is used to treat mild to moderate  caused by .</p>
<p>Aricept is not a cure for Alzheimer's disease. This condition will progress over time, even in people who take donepezil.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Before taking Aricept, tell your doctor if you have a heart rhythm disorder such as "sick sinus syndrome" (slow heartbeats), an enlarged prostate, urination problems, asthma, obstructive pulmonary disease, or a seizure disorder such as epilepsy.</p>
<p>If you need to have any type of surgery, tell the surgeon ahead of time that you are taking Aricept.</p>
<p>Aricept can cause side effects that may impair your thinking or reactions. Be careful if you drive or do anything that requires you to be awake and alert.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not use Aricept if you are allergic to donepezil or certain other drugs. Tell your doctor if you are allergic to any medicines.</p>
<p>To make sure Aricept is safe for you, tell your doctor if you have:</p>
<p>a heart rhythm disorder;</p>
<p>a history of stomach ulcers;</p>
<p>an enlarged prostate or urination problems;</p>
<p>liver or kidney disease;</p>
<p>epilepsy or other seizure disorder;</p>
<p>trouble swallowing; or</p>
<p>asthma, chronic obstructive pulmonary disease (COPD), or other breathing disorder.</p>
<p>It is not known whether Aricept will harm an unborn baby. Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or plan to become pregnant while using this medicine.</p>
<p>It is not known whether donepezil passes into breast milk or if it could harm a nursing baby. Tell your doctor if you are breast-feeding a baby.</p>
<h2>How should I take Aricept?</h2>
<p>Take Aricept exactly as it was prescribed for you. Follow all directions on your prescription label. Do not take this medicine in larger or smaller amounts or for longer than recommended.</p>
<p>You may take Aricept with or without food.</p>
<p>Do not crush, chew, or break the <b>regular tablet</b>. Swallow it whole.</p>
<b>regular tablet</b>
<p>To take the orally disintegrating tablet (Aricept ODT):</p>
<p>Keep the tablet in its blister pack until you are ready to take it. Open the package and peel or cut the backing from the tablet blister. Do not push a tablet through the backing or you may damage the tablet.</p>
<p>Use dry hands to remove the tablet and place it in your mouth.</p>
<p>Do not swallow the tablet whole. Allow it to dissolve in your mouth without chewing.</p>
<p>Swallow several times as the tablet dissolves. After the tablet dissolves completely, drink a glass of water.</p>
<p>If you need surgery or dental work, tell the surgeon ahead of time that you are using Aricept. You may need to stop using the medicine for a short time.</p>
<p>You should not stop using Aricept without your doctor's advice.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture and heat.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">Dosing information</h2>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose for Alzheimer's Disease:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose for Alzheimer's Disease:</b>
<p>Initial dose: 5 mg orally once a day, in the evening prior to retiring<br/>
<br/>
Mild to moderate Alzheimer's disease:<br/>
-Maintenance dose: 10 mg orally once a day, after the patient has been on an initial dose of 5 mg once a day for 4 to 6 weeks<br/>
<br/>
Moderate to severe Alzheimer's disease:<br/>
-Maintenance dose: 23 mg orally once a day, after the patient has been on a dose of 10 mg once a day for at least 3 months<br/>
<br/>
Comments: A higher dose of 10 mg may or may not provide a statistically significantly greater clinical benefit than a 5 mg dose. Prescriber and patient's preference should be considered.<br/>
<br/>
Uses: For mild, moderate, and severe Alzheimer's type dementia</p>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Take the missed dose as soon as you remember. Skip the missed dose if it is almost time for your next scheduled dose. Do not take extra medicine to make up the missed dose.</p>
<p>If you miss your doses for more than 7 days in a row, call your doctor before taking the medicine again.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222.</p>
<p>Overdose symptoms may include severe nausea, vomiting, drooling, sweating, blurred vision, feeling light-headed, slow heartbeat, shallow breathing, muscle weakness, fainting, or seizure (convulsions).</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What to avoid</h2>
<p>This medicine may impair your thinking or reactions. Be careful if you drive or do anything that requires you to be alert.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="side-effects">Aricept side effects</h2>
<p>Get emergency medical help if you have <b>signs of an allergic reaction to Aricept</b>: hives; difficult breathing; swelling of your face, lips, tongue, or throat.</p>
<b>signs of an allergic reaction to Aricept</b>
<p>Stop using Aricept and call your doctor at once if you have:</p>
<p>severe or ongoing vomiting;</p>
<p>a light-headed feeling, like you might pass out;</p>
<p>slow heartbeats;</p>
<p>seizure (convulsions);</p>
<p>painful or difficult urination;</p>
<p>new or worsening breathing problems; or</p>
<p>signs of stomach bleeding--severe heartburn or stomach pain, bloody or tarry stools, coughing up blood or vomit that looks like coffee grounds.</p>
<p>Common Aricept side effects may include:</p>
<p>nausea, vomiting, diarrhea;</p>
<p>loss of appetite;</p>
<p>muscle pain;</p>
<p>sleep problems (insomnia); or</p>
<p>feeling tired;.</p>
<p>This is not a complete list of side effects and others may occur. Call your doctor for medical advice about side effects. You may report side effects to FDA at 1-800-FDA-1088.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="interactions">What other drugs will affect Aricept?</h2>
<p>Tell your doctor about all medicines you use, and those you start or stop using during your treatment with Aricept, especially:</p>
<p>NSAIDs (nonsteroidal anti-inflammatory drugs)--aspirin, ibuprofen (Advil, Motrin), naproxen (Aleve), celecoxib, diclofenac, indomethacin, meloxicam, and others;</p>
<p>This list is not complete. Other drugs may interact with donepezil, including prescription and over-the-counter medicines, vitamins, and herbal products. Not all possible interactions are listed in this medication guide.</p>
<h2>More about Aricept (donepezil)</h2>
<h2>Further information</h2>
<p>Remember, keep this and all other medicines out of the reach of children, never share your medicines with others, and use Aricept only for the indication prescribed.</p>

Aripiprazole:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b> aripiprazole (AR i PIP ra zole)<br/>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is aripiprazole?</h2>
<p> is an antipsychotic medicine that is used to treat the symptoms of psychotic conditions such as  and  (manic ). It is not known if aripiprazole is safe or effective in children younger than 13 with schizophrenia, or children younger than 10 with bipolar disorder.</p>
<p>Aripiprazole is also used together with other medicines to treat  in adults.</p>
<p>Aripiprazole is also used in children 6 years or older who have Tourette's disorder, or symptoms of autistic disorder (irritability, aggression, mood swings, temper tantrums, and self-injury).</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Aripiprazole is not approved for use in older adults with -related psychosis.</p>
<p>Some people have thoughts about suicide while taking aripiprazole. Stay alert to changes in your mood or symptoms. Report any new or worsening symptoms to your doctor.</p>
<p>Do not stop using aripiprazole suddenly, or you could have unpleasant withdrawal symptoms.</p>
<p>Avoid driving and doing other tasks or actions that call for you to be alert or have clear eyesight until you see how aripiprazole affects you.</p>
<p>High blood sugar or diabetes, high cholesterol, and weight gain have happened with drugs like this one. These may raise the chance of heart and brain blood vessel disease.</p>
<p>Low white blood cell counts have happened with drugs like this one. This may lead to a higher chance of infection. Rarely, infections have been deadly. Tell your doctor if you have ever had a low white blood cell count. Call your doctor right away if you have signs of infection like fever, chills, or sore throat.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not take aripiprazole if you are allergic to it.</p>
<p>Aripiprazole may increase the risk of death in older adults with dementia-related psychosis and is not approved for this use.</p>
<p>To make sure aripiprazole is safe for you, tell your doctor if you have ever had:</p>
<p>liver or kidney disease;</p>
<p>heart disease, high or , heart rhythm problems;</p>
<p> or triglycerides (a type of fat in the blood);</p>
<p>low white blood cell (WBC) counts;</p>
<p>a  or stroke;</p>
<p> or ;</p>
<p>trouble swallowing;</p>
<p>diabetes (in you or a family member); or</p>
<p>obsessive-compulsive disorder, impulse-control disorder, or addictive behaviors.</p>
<p>Some people have thoughts about suicide while taking aripiprazole. Your doctor will need to check your progress at regular visits. Your family or other caregivers should also be alert to changes in your mood or symptoms.</p>
<p>The liquid form (oral solution) of this medication may contain up to 15 grams of sugar per dose. Before taking aripiprazole oral solution, tell your doctor if you have diabetes.</p>
<p>Aripiprazole may cause you to have high blood sugar (hyperglycemia). If you are diabetic, check your blood sugar levels on a regular basis while you are taking aripiprazole.</p>
<p>The orally disintegrating tablet form of this medication may contain over 3 milligrams of phenylalanine per tablet. Before taking  Discmelt, tell your doctor if you have .</p>
<p><b>Taking antipsychotic medicine in the last 3 months of pregnancy may cause problems in the newborn</b>, such as withdrawal symptoms, breathing problems, feeding problems, fussiness, tremors, and limp or stiff muscles. However, you may have withdrawal symptoms or other problems if you stop taking your medicine during pregnancy. <b>If you become pregnant, do not stop taking aripiprazole without your doctor's advice.</b></p>
<b>Taking antipsychotic medicine in the last 3 months of pregnancy may cause problems in the newborn</b>
<b>If you become pregnant, do not stop taking aripiprazole without your doctor's advice.</b>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="faq">Popular FAQ</h2>
<p>Abilify (aripiprazole) and Vraylar (cariprazine) are both classified as atypical antipsychotic medications. They help to treat several mental health conditions, including schizophrenia and bipolar disorder. They both affect chemicals in the brain such as serotonin and dopamine to help stabilize mood, thoughts and behaviors. </p>
<p>The main differences between Abilify and Abilify Maintena are how they are supplied, how they are administered, their FDA-approved uses and their costs. They both contain the active ingredient aripiprazole, an atypical antipsychotic, and are approved for the treatment of schizophrenia and bipolar disorder. </p>
<p>The oral tablet formulation Abilify MyCite (aripiprazole) is embedded with the ingestible Proteus sensor that allows patients, and, if given access, doctors and caregivers, to track ingestion of the Abilify medication on a smartphone or web-based portal. The system sends a message from the pillâ€™s sensor to a wearable patch on the patient, which then transmits to the device. </p>

Ascorbic acid:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b> ascorbic acid (vitamin C) (as KORE bik AS id)<br/><b>Brand Name:</b> <i>Acerola, Ascorbic Acid Quick Melts, C/Rose Hips, Cecon, Cemill 500, C-Time, Ester-C, N Ice with Vitamin C, Sunkist Vitamin C, Vasoflex HD, Vicks Vitamin C Drops, Vitamin C, <span id="all_brands" style="display: none;">Cenolate, Mega-C-Acid Plus, Cee-500, C-500-Gr, Centrum Singles-Vitamin C, Ascot, Cevi-Bid, Vitamin C TR, Vitamin C with Rose Hips, Cemill 1000, Ascor L NC, Ascor</span></i><br/><b>Dosage Forms:</b> oral capsule (500 mg); oral gum (250 mg); oral liquid (500 mg/5 mL; 90 mg/mL); oral tablet (100 mg; 1000 mg; 1500 mg; 250 mg; 500 mg; with bioflavonoids; with bioflavonoids 500 mg); oral tablet, chewable (100 mg; 25 mg; 250 mg; 500 mg; 60 mg); oral tablet, disintegrating (100 mg; 250 mg); oral tablet, extended release (1000 mg)</p>

<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is ascorbic acid?</h2>
<p>Ascorbic acid () occurs naturally in foods such as citrus fruit, tomatoes, potatoes, and leafy vegetables. Vitamin C is important for bones and connective tissues, muscles, and blood vessels. Vitamin C also helps the body absorb iron, which is needed for red blood cell production.</p>
<p>Ascorbic acid is used to treat and prevent vitamin C deficiency.</p>
<p>Ascorbic acid may also be used for purposes not listed in this medication guide.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>Follow all directions on your medicine label and package. Tell each of your healthcare providers about all your medical conditions, , and all medicines you use.</p>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>You should not use ascorbic acid if you have ever had an allergic reaction to a vitamin C supplement.</p>
<p>Ask a doctor or pharmacist about using ascorbic acid if you have:</p>
<p>kidney disease or a history of ;</p>
<p>hereditary iron overload disorder (hematochromatosis); or</p>
<p>if you smoke ( can make ascorbic acid less effective).</p>
<p>Your dose needs may be different during pregnancy or while you are breast-feeding a baby. Do not use ascorbic acid without your doctor's advice in either case.</p>
<h2>How should I take ascorbic acid?</h2>
<p>Use exactly as directed on the label, or as prescribed by your doctor. Do not use in larger or smaller amounts or for longer than recommended.</p>
<p>The recommended dietary allowance of vitamin C (ascorbic acid) increases with age. Follow your healthcare provider's instructions. You may also consult the Office of Dietary Supplements of the National Institutes of Health, or the U.S. Department of Agriculture (USDA) Nutrient Database (formerly "Recommended Daily Allowances") listings for more information.</p>
<p>Drink plenty of liquids while you are taking ascorbic acid.</p>
<p>The chewable tablet must be chewed before you swallow it.</p>
<p>Ascorbic acid gum may be chewed as long as desired and then thrown away.</p>
<p>Do not crush, chew, or break an <b>extended-release tablet</b>. Swallow it whole.</p>
<b>extended-release tablet</b>
<p>Measure liquid medicine with a special dose-measuring spoon or medicine cup. If you do not have a dose-measuring device, ask your pharmacist for one.</p>
<p>Keep the orally disintegrating tablet in the package until you are ready to take it. Use dry hands to remove the tablet and place it in your mouth. Do not swallow the tablet whole. Allow it to dissolve in your mouth without chewing. Swallow several times as the tablet dissolves.</p>
<p>Store ascorbic acid at room temperature away from moisture and heat.</p>
<p><b>Do not stop using ascorbic acid suddenly after long-term use at high doses,</b> or you could have "conditional" vitamin C deficiency. Symptoms include bleeding gums, feeling very tired, and red or blue pinpoint spots around your hair follicles. Follow your doctor's instructions about tapering your dose. Conditional vitamin C deficiency can be difficult to correct without medical supervision.</p>
<b>Do not stop using ascorbic acid suddenly after long-term use at high doses,</b>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Take the missed dose as soon as you remember. Skip the missed dose if it is almost time for your next scheduled dose. Do not take extra medicine to make up the missed dose.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What should I avoid while taking ascorbic acid?</h2>
<p>Follow your doctor's instructions about any restrictions on food, beverages, or activity.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="side-effects">Ascorbic acid side effects</h2>
<p>Get emergency medical help if you have any of these <b>signs of an allergic reaction:</b> ; difficult breathing; swelling of your face, lips, tongue, or throat.</p>
<b>signs of an allergic reaction:</b>
<p>Stop using ascorbic acid and call your doctor at once if you have:</p>
<p>joint pain, weakness or tired feeling, , stomach pain;</p>
<p>chills, fever, increased urge to urinate, painful or difficult urination; or</p>
<p>severe pain in your side or lower back, blood in your urine.</p>
<p>Common side effects may include:</p>
<p>, ; or</p>
<p>, , stomach cramps.</p>
<p>This is not a complete list of side effects and others may occur. Call your doctor for medical advice about side effects. You may report side effects to FDA at 1-800-FDA-1088.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">Ascorbic acid dosing information</h2>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose for Dietary Supplement:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose for Dietary Supplement:</b>
<p>Oral, IM, IV, subcutaneously: 50 to 200 mg/day.</p>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose for Urinary Acidification:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose for Urinary Acidification:</b>
<p>Oral, IM, IV, subcutaneously: 4 to 12 g/day in 3 to 4 divided doses.</p>
<p><b>Usual Adult Dose for Scurvy:</b></p>
<b>Usual Adult Dose for Scurvy:</b>
<p>Oral, IM, IV, subcutaneously: 100 to 250 mg once or twice daily for a minimum of two weeks.</p>
<p><b>Usual Pediatric Dose for Dietary Supplement:</b></p>
<b>Usual Pediatric Dose for Dietary Supplement:</b>
<p>Oral, IM, IV, subcutaneously: 35 to 100 mg/day.</p>
<p><b>Usual Pediatric Dose for Urinary Acidification:</b></p>
<b>Usual Pediatric Dose for Urinary Acidification:</b>
<p>Oral, IM, IV, subcutaneously: 500 mg every 6 to 8 hours.</p>
<p><b>Usual Pediatric Dose for Scurvy:</b></p>
<b>Usual Pediatric Dose for Scurvy:</b>
<p>Oral, IM, IV, subcutaneously: 100 to 300 mg/day in divided doses for a minimum of two weeks.</p>

<p>Other drugs may interact with ascorbic acid, including prescription and over-the-counter medicines, , and . Tell each of your health care providers about all medicines you use now and any medicine you start or stop using.</p>

Aspirin:
 <p class="drug-subtitle"><b>Generic Name:</b> aspirin (oral) (AS pir in)<br/>
<b>Brand Name:</b> <i>Arthritis Pain, Aspi-Cor, Aspir 81, Aspir-Low, Bayer Plus, Bufferin, Durlaza, Ecotrin, Ecpirin, Miniprin.</i></p>
<b>Generic Name:</b>
<b>Brand Name:</b>
<p class="ddc-reviewed-by"><span>Medically reviewed by . Last updated on Oct 1, 2020.</span></p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="uses">What is aspirin?</h2>
<p>Aspirin is a salicylate (sa-LIS-il-ate). It works by reducing substances in the body that cause , , and inflammation.</p>
<p>Aspirin is used to treat pain, and reduce fever or inflammation. It is sometimes used to treat or prevent heart attacks, strokes, and chest pain (angina).</p>
<p>Aspirin should be used for cardiovascular conditions only under the supervision of a doctor.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="warnings">Warnings</h2>
<p>You should not use aspirin if you have a bleeding disorder such as hemophilia, a recent history of stomach or intestinal bleeding, or if you are allergic to an NSAID (non-steroidal anti-inflammatory drug) such as Advil, Motrin, Aleve, Orudis, Indocin, Lodine, Voltaren, Toradol, Mobic, Relafen, Feldene, and others.</p>
<p>Do not give this medication to a child or teenager with a fever, flu symptoms, or chickenpox. <b>Salicylates can cause Reye's syndrome, a serious and sometimes fatal condition in children.</b></p>
<b>Salicylates can cause Reye's syndrome, a serious and sometimes fatal condition in children.</b>
<h2>Before taking this medicine</h2>
<p>Do not give this medicine to a child or teenager with a fever, flu symptoms, or chickenpox. <b>Aspirin can cause Reye's syndrome, a serious and sometimes fatal condition in children.</b></p>
<b>Aspirin can cause Reye's syndrome, a serious and sometimes fatal condition in children.</b>
<p>You should not use aspirin if you are allergic to it, or if you have:</p>
<p>a recent history of stomach or intestinal bleeding;</p>
<p>a bleeding disorder such as hemophilia; or</p>
<p>if you have ever had an asthma attack or severe allergic reaction after taking aspirin or an NSAID (non-steroidal anti-inflammatory drug) such as Advil, Motrin, Aleve, Orudis, Indocin, Lodine, Voltaren, Toradol, Mobic, Relafen, Feldene, and others.</p>
<p>To make sure this medicine is safe for you, tell your doctor if you have:</p>
<p>asthma or seasonal allergies;</p>
<p>stomach ulcers;</p>
<p>liver disease;</p>
<p>kidney disease;</p>
<p>a bleeding or blood clotting disorder;</p>
<p>gout; or</p>
<p>heart disease, high blood pressure, or congestive heart failure.</p>
<p><b>Taking aspirin during late pregnancy may cause bleeding in the mother or the baby during delivery.</b> Tell your doctor if you are pregnant or plan to become pregnant.</p>
<b>Taking aspirin during late pregnancy may cause bleeding in the mother or the baby during delivery.</b>
<p>Aspirin can pass into breast milk and may harm a nursing baby. You should not breastfeed while using this medicine.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="dosage">How should I take aspirin?</h2>
<p>Take aspirin exactly as directed on the label, or as prescribed by your doctor. Do not use in larger or smaller amounts or for longer than recommended.</p>
<p>Always follow directions on the medicine label about giving aspirin to a child.</p>
<p>Take with food if aspirin upsets your stomach.</p>
<p>You must chew the <b>chewable tablet</b> before you swallow it.</p>
<b>chewable tablet</b>
<p>Do not crush, chew, break, or open an <b>enteric-coated</b> or <b>delayed/extended-release</b> pill. Swallow the pill whole.</p>
<b>enteric-coated</b>
<b>delayed/extended-release</b>
<p>If you need surgery, tell the surgeon ahead of time that you are using this medicine. You may need to stop using it for a short time.</p>
<p>Do not use aspirin if you smell a strong vinegar odor in the bottle. The medicine may no longer be effective.</p>
<p>Store at room temperature away from moisture and heat.</p>
<h2>What happens if I miss a dose?</h2>
<p>Since aspirin is used when needed, you may not be on a dosing schedule. If you are on a schedule, use the missed dose as soon as you remember. Skip the missed dose if it is almost time for your next scheduled dose. Do not use extra medicine to make up the missed dose.</p>
<h2>What happens if I overdose?</h2>
<p>Seek emergency medical attention or call the Poison Help line at 1-800-222-1222.</p>
<p>Overdose symptoms may include stomach pain, vomiting, diarrhea, vision or hearing problems, fast or slow breathing, or confusion.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="what-to-avoid">What to avoid</h2>
<p>Avoid drinking alcohol while you are taking aspirin. Heavy drinking can increase your risk of stomach bleeding.</p>
<p>If you are taking this medicine to prevent heart attack or stroke, avoid also taking ibuprofen (Advil, Motrin). Ibuprofen may make this medicine less effective in protecting your heart and blood vessels. If you must use both medications, ask your doctor how far apart your doses should be.</p>
<p>Ask a doctor or pharmacist before using any cold, allergy, or pain medication. Many medicines available over the counter contain aspirin or an NSAID. Taking certain products together can cause you to get too much of this type of medication. Check the label to see if a medicine contains aspirin, ibuprofen, ketoprofen, naproxen, or an NSAID.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="side-effects">Aspirin side effects</h2>
<p>Get emergency medical help if you have <b>signs of an allergic reaction to aspirin</b>: hives; difficult breathing; swelling of your face, lips, tongue, or throat.</p>
<b>signs of an allergic reaction to aspirin</b>
<p>Stop using this medicine and call your doctor at once if you have:</p>
<p>ringing in your ears, confusion, hallucinations, rapid breathing, seizure (convulsions);</p>
<p>severe nausea, vomiting, or stomach pain;</p>
<p>bloody or tarry stools, coughing up blood or vomit that looks like coffee grounds;</p>
<p>fever lasting longer than 3 days; or</p>
<p>swelling, or pain lasting longer than 10 days.</p>
<p>Common aspirin side effects may include:</p>
<p>upset stomach, heartburn;</p>
<p>drowsiness; or</p>
<p>mild headache.</p>
<p>This is not a complete list of side effects and others may occur. Call your doctor for medical advice about side effects. You may report side effects to FDA at 1-800-FDA-1088.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="interactions">What other drugs will affect aspirin?</h2>
<p>Ask your doctor before using aspirin if you take an antidepressant such as citalopram, escitalopram, fluoxetine (Prozac), fluvoxamine, paroxetine, sertraline (Zoloft), trazodone, or vilazodone. Taking any of these medicines with an NSAID may cause you to bruise or bleed easily.</p>
<p>Ask a doctor or pharmacist if it is safe for you to use aspirin if you are also using any of the following drugs:</p>
<p>a blood thinner (warfarin, Coumadin, Jantoven), or other medication used to prevent blood clots; or</p>
<p>other salicylates such as Nuprin Backache Caplet, Kaopectate, KneeRelief, Pamprin Cramp Formula, Pepto-Bismol, Tricosal, Trilisate, and others.</p>
<p>This list is not complete. Other drugs may interact with aspirin, including prescription and over-the-counter medicines, vitamins, and herbal products. Not all possible interactions are listed in this medication guide.</p>
<h2 class="ddc-anchor-offset" id="faq">Popular FAQ</h2>
<p>Aspirin may help menstrual pain. It is in a group of drugs called salicylates. It works by reducing substances in the body that cause pain, fever, and inflammation. Aspirin is used to treat mild to moderate pain, and also to reduce fever or inflammation. It is best taken with food and a glass of water.</p>
<h2>More about aspirin</h2>
<h2>Further information</h2>
<p>Remember, keep this and all other medicines out of the reach of children, never share your medicines with others, and use aspirin only for the indication prescribed.</p>
<p class="ddc-disclaimer">Always consult your healthcare provider to ensure the information displayed on this page applies to your personal circumstances.</p>
